Current Commentary

The Two Major Issues of the Present 24

— Year

Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, the British economic envoy, recently issued a lengthy farewell speech. While some points, such as his statement on the attitude of the Japanese authorities towards China's tariff issue and his discussion of China's reduction of import tariff rates, are debatable, the good intentions of the entire article are deeply felt. We are particularly touched by the two issues of Chinese security and the special situation in North China mentioned by Sir Frederick. Please elaborate.

Sir Frederick Leith-Ross said, "The future of China's currency and even its entire financial standing will depend, first, on the maintenance of security in the Chinese interior, and second, on the resolution of the special situation in North China." In the original text, due to the speaker's position, only these two major issues of the present were mentioned without further elaboration. In fact, in our observation, the importance of these two issues surpasses the other parts noted and elaborated upon by Leith-Ross. They are related to the safety and danger of China, and currency and finance are only one aspect of their concerns.

At present, the issue of domestic security other than resisting invasion and suppressing bandits, although the news is constantly changing and people are frightened and disheartened, only two weeks have passed since the Second Plenary Session. A peaceful resolution may be hoped for, and the joint telegram from Song and Han expressing their sincere concern to the Central Government is also sufficient to ease the situation and alert those intending to start a war. Furthermore, the public opinion against civil war has become consistent, and those involved should read the words "national ruin is imminent" and repent. The consistent public opinion is also sufficient to exert a restraining effect. Those who violate the consistent public opinion will fail. The past is like this and can be a lesson.

The special situation in North China involves political and diplomatic issues and economic issues. Now, based on the meaning of Leith-Ross's speech, focusing on the issue of smuggling related to the economy, Leith-Ross lightly believed the exhortations of one party, so he hoped that various difficulties could be resolved. However, the reporter observes the rampant attacks of smuggled goods on the market and the obstruction encountered by anti-smuggling efforts, believing that it is not enough for the people to have the determination to stop smuggled goods on their own to promote the resolution of difficulties. Now the government has issued strict punishment regulations. The crime of tax evasion is punishable by death for serious offenses, and those over 1,000 yuan are subject to life imprisonment. There is no way to add to the severity of the prohibition. Only by hoping that the general public can assist in the implementation of the law and jointly reject smuggled goods to maintain legitimate commerce, will the smugglers' skills be exhausted, and the smuggling problem will not be difficult to resolve as Leith-Ross said.

Sir Frederick Leith-Ross came to investigate China's financial and economic difficulties and to determine the possibility of assisting China in overcoming these difficulties, so his statements are generally focused on currency and finance. However, the two prerequisites he mentioned in conjunction with these issues can only be effectively resolved with public opinion and public power. We hope that the people of the country will know that their own strength is reliable and make efforts accordingly.

Regulations for the Implementation of the National Assembly Representative Election Law (Draft) 25

(Nanjing) The draft Regulations for the Implementation of the National Assembly Representative Election Law was passed at the Executive Yuan meeting on the 23rd. The original draft is as follows:

Chapter 1: General Provisions

Article 1: These Regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 61 of the National Assembly Representative Election Law (hereinafter referred to as the "Election Law").

Article 2: Voters must present their citizen certificates when voting.

Article 3: Township, town, and neighborhood public offices shall compile citizen registers of male and female citizens within their jurisdiction who have taken the oath and received citizen certificates. These registers shall be submitted level by level to the provincial offices for review and announcement one month before voting.

Article 4: The announcement period for the voter register shall be three days. If a person believes there is an error or omission, they may request a correction within the announcement period.

Article 5: Professional voters who have more than one voting right shall, 20 days before the election, declare their intention to participate in the election of a specific group and the election authority they decide to participate in shall notify other election authorities. If they fail to do so within the deadline, the election supervisor shall designate it.

Article 6: When nominating candidates for various elections, the ancestral home of the nominee shall be indicated on the ballot. After the candidates are determined, the election supervisor shall compile a register of their names, ages, ancestral homes, experiences, and occupations and submit it to the General Election Office, which shall forward it to the National Government for designation and then distribute it to the election supervisors for public announcement.

Article 7: The full names of all candidates designated by the National Government for each type of election shall be listed on the ballot, arranged in order by the number of strokes in their surnames, from fewest to most.

Article 8: If a person is elected as a candidate in both a regional election and a professional election, or in two professional group elections, they shall choose one. The vacancy shall be filled by the alternate representative of that region or group in accordance with the law. If the number of votes is the same, it shall be determined by drawing lots.

Article 9: The age of voters and candidates shall be calculated as of the date of register compilation. The years of practice or service of candidates in professional groups shall be calculated as of the date of nomination.

Chapter 2: Regional Elections

Article 10: The election supervisor shall periodically notify the magistrates and mayors within the region to compile and submit registers containing the following information within the specified time limit, which shall be forwarded to the chief election supervisor for review: 1. The division of each county into townships and towns or the division of each city into neighborhoods; 2. The full names and resumes of all township and town heads or neighborhood heads.

Article 11: The election supervisor of each region shall allocate the number of candidates to be produced by each county under its jurisdiction in proportion to the number of citizens in each county, and report it level by level to the General Election Office for verification and public announcement.

Article 12: The nomination of candidates shall be conducted jointly by the township and town heads (or neighborhood heads in cities) in each electoral district, based on the number of representatives to be produced in that district, using a signed, joint nomination method (for example, if the number of representatives from the first district of Jiangsu is the same, each township or town head in that district may use the same election ballot to nominate four people, not limited to those with ancestry in the county). The election office of each election district shall count the ballots. According to the allocation in the previous article, the candidates with the most votes in each county shall be the candidates. In counties without township or town heads, the Lianbao Director or equivalent personnel shall exercise the nomination rights.

Article 13: The nomination of candidates shall be conducted at the district public office in each county. In counties without district public offices, it shall be conducted in a public place.

Article 14: A candidate who works or resides elsewhere but has not changed their ancestral home may still be a candidate for the region to which their ancestral home belongs.

Article 15: The candidates nominated by each electoral district shall be submitted to the General Election Office for review after the provincial government has signed and commented on them.

Article 16: The candidates nominated by cities directly under the Executive Yuan shall be submitted by the mayors to the General Election Office for review.

Chapter 3: Professional Elections

Article 17: The "legally established organizations" mentioned in Article 19 of Chapter 3 of the Election Law are limited to those that have been registered with the local competent authority.

Article 18: The organs of the lowest-level organizations in professional groups are as follows: 1. Farmers' associations: the township farmers' associations to which they belong in counties, and the district farmers' associations in cities; 2. Labor unions: the industry labor unions to which they belong; 3. Chambers of commerce: the industry trade associations to which they belong.

Article 19: Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Jiangsu Province stipulated in Schedule 3 of the Election Law, one representative shall be from the Beijing-Shanghai-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Hubei Province, one representative shall be from the Ping-Han Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Hunan Province, one representative shall be from the Yue-Han Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Hebei Province, one representative shall be from the Beijing-Shenyang Railway Labor Union, and one representative shall be from the Ping-Sui Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Shandong Province, one representative shall be from the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Shanxi Province, one representative shall be from the Zhengtai Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Henan Province, one representative shall be from the Longhai Railway Labor Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Shanghai Municipality, one representative shall be from the Chinese Seamen's Union. Within the quota of representatives of labor unions in Guangdong Province, one representative shall be from the Chinese Seamen's Union.

Article 20: The election supervisor shall periodically notify the organizations within the region to compile and submit registers containing the following information within the specified time limit, which shall be forwarded to the chief election supervisor for review: 1. The organizational charter, establishment procedures, and their processes; 2. The registration authority and the date of registration; 3. The officers and their experiences; 4. The names, ages, ancestral homes, and years of engagement in the profession of the members; 5. If a member is also a member of another organization, the name of the other organization and the organization selected in accordance with the last paragraph of Article 5 of the Election Law.

Article 21: The officers of professional group organizations shall nominate candidates in accordance with the number of representatives to be elected by each organization, using a signed, joint nomination method, at the location designated by the election supervisor. The ballots shall be sent to the location designated by the chief election supervisor for counting and forwarded to the election office for review.

Article 22: The chief election supervisor of free professional groups shall periodically notify the organizations to compile and submit registers containing the following information within the specified time limit: 1. The organizational charter, establishment procedures, and their processes; 2. The registration authority and the date of registration; 3. The officers and their experiences; 4. The names, ages, ancestral homes, residences, and years of engagement in the profession of the members; 5. If a member is also a member of another organization, the name of the other organization and the organization selected in accordance with the last paragraph of Article 5 of the Election Law.

Article 23: The officers of free professional group organizations shall nominate candidates in accordance with the number of representatives to be elected by each organization, using a signed, joint nomination method, by mail. The ballots shall be sent through the competent administrative authority to the location designated by the chief election supervisor for counting and forwarded to the General Election Office for review.

Chapter 4: Special Elections

Article 24: Citizens in the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe shall take the oath at their respective local governments in accordance with the provisions of Article 5 of the Citizen Oath Registration Rules. Those who are residing in various provinces and have household registration books before June of this year as a basis and have taken the citizen oath may elect in accordance with the law (the election certificate shall be used in place of the citizen certificate). Those who do not have household registration to rely on shall also obtain reliable proof.

Article 25: The allocation of the nine representatives stipulated in the first paragraph of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be as follows: two from the Xilin Gol League and the eight banners of Chahar, four from the Urad and Dorbod Leagues, the Smed Banner, and the four banners of Suidong, one from the Alxa and Ejine Banners, and two from the left and right wings of the Qinghai League.

Article 26: The division of electoral districts stipulated in the first and second paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law may be adjusted by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet according to the convenience of the original administrative regions of each league, banner, and tribe, and submitted to the General Election Office for approval.

Article 27: The number of representative candidates to be nominated by each league, banner, and tribe within the first paragraph of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be ninety. The allocation method is as follows: 1. The Xilin Gol, Chahar, Urad, and Dorbod Leagues shall each nominate twelve representative candidates, for a total of forty-eight; 2. The left and right wings of the Qinghai League shall each nominate nine representative candidates, for a total of eighteen; 3. The Alxa, Ejine, and Smed special banners shall each nominate six representative candidates, for a total of eighteen; 4. The four banners of Suidong shall jointly nominate six representative candidates. The number of representative candidates to be nominated by each league within the second paragraph of the same article shall be thirty. The allocation method is as follows: 1. Eight from the Bayantu Setgeltu Chun League; 2. Twelve from the Ünen Sükhütü League; 3. Ten from the Qingseltu League.

Article 28: The representative candidates to be nominated by each league, banner, and tribe within the first and second paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be nominated jointly by the Jasagh to which each league belongs, according to the prescribed number, and the representative candidates to be nominated by each banner shall be nominated jointly by the Thamji and Tusalags to which they belong, according to the prescribed number, and submitted by the election supervisor of each to the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet for signing and commenting, and then submitted to the General Election Office for review and forwarded to the National Government for designation before being elected in accordance with the law.

Article 29: The election of representatives from each league, banner, and tribe within the first and second paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be handled by the election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet ordering each election supervisor to follow the regional election procedures according to the number of candidates designated by the National Government.

Article 30: The representative candidates stipulated in the third and fourth paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be allocated by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet according to the actual situation, and a list shall be prepared, with comments signed, and submitted to the General Election Office for review and forwarded to the National Government for designation.

Article 31: The election of representatives stipulated in the third and fourth paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be conducted by Mongolians residing in various places who have citizen certificates, voting at the locations designated by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet. If voters cannot come to vote in person, they may send the ballot directly to the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet.

Article 32: The number of representatives stipulated in the first paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be allocated by the Kashag according to the situation in various parts of Tibet.

Article 33: The representative candidates stipulated in the first paragraph of Article 33 of the Election Law shall be reported by the Kashag after being nominated by various places and submitted to the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet for signing and commenting, and then submitted to the General Election Office for review and forwarded to the National Government for designation.

Article 34: The election of representatives stipulated in the first paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be handled by the election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet ordering the Kashag to follow the regional election procedures according to the number of candidates designated by the National Government.

Article 35: The "Tibetan people" mentioned in the second paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law refer to Tibetan people temporarily residing in various places.

Article 36: The representative candidates stipulated in the second paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be nominated by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet from Tibetan people residing in various places who have citizen certificates, and a list shall be prepared, with comments signed, and submitted to the General Election Office for review and forwarded to the National Government for designation.

Article 37: The election of representatives stipulated in the second paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be conducted by Tibetans residing in various places who have citizen certificates, voting at the locations designated by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet. If voters cannot come to vote in person, they may send the ballot directly to the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet.

Article 38: The qualifications of voters, nominators, and candidates among overseas Chinese shall be reviewed by the election supervisor and then the following registers shall be convened separately and reported to the chief election supervisor for review. The register of candidates shall be forwarded by the election supervisor to the General Election Office for review. 1. The voter register shall record the name, age, ancestral home, residence, and occupation of each voter; 2. The register of organization members and officers shall record the type of organization, organizational structure, establishment process, and the name, age, ancestral home, residence, and position of each member and full-time officer of the organization; 3. The candidate register shall record the name, age, ancestral home, residence, and years of engagement in the profession of the candidate, or the years of membership in the association.

Article 39: The nomination of candidates among overseas Chinese shall be conducted at the location of the election supervisor.

Article 40: The nomination of candidates among overseas Chinese shall be conducted by the officers of the organizations recognized by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission.

Article 41: Candidates among overseas Chinese shall have the following qualifications: 1. Have the qualifications of a voter; 2. Be at least 25 years old; 3. Have been a member of the organization for more than three years. If it is a professional group, have been engaged in the profession for more than three years and are currently a member of the organization.

Article 42: The qualification of nominators in overseas Chinese organizations shall be limited to the current officers of the organization. The number of candidates shall be three times the number of representatives to be produced in the area.

Article 43: If there are special circumstances in the nomination and election of overseas Chinese, the local election supervisor may be asked to conduct the election by mail.

Article 44: If there are obstacles to the nomination and election of overseas Chinese due to special circumstances, and the local election supervisor cannot resolve them, the matter shall be reported to the chief election supervisor and forwarded to the General Election Office for handling.

Article 45: The nomination of candidates in the military shall be handled by the highest-ranking officer of each election unit.

Article 46: The nomination procedures in the previous article shall be stipulated by the chief election supervisor of the military.

Article 47: After the candidates in each election unit are selected, they shall be sent to the Military Affairs Commission for signing and commenting, and then forwarded to the General Election Office for review and submission to the National Government for designation of ninety candidates.

Article 48: The election in the previous article shall be conducted at the location of each election unit.

Article 49: If a person is elected in both a regional election and a military election, they shall apply to choose one. The vacancy shall be filled by the alternate representative of that region or military in accordance with the law.

Chapter 5: Election Offices and Election Supervisors

Article 50: The organizational regulations for various election offices shall be formulated by the General Election Office. Various election offices shall be dissolved immediately after the election is completed.

Article 51: The detailed rules for various election offices, polling stations, and ballot counting stations shall be formulated by the election supervisor and reported to the General Election Office for record.

Article 52: The results of the election supervisor's review of candidate qualifications shall be reported to the General Election Office for approval.

Article 53: The establishment of election supervisors stipulated in the first and second paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be handled by the General Election Office appointing the highest administrative officers of each electoral district delineated by the chief election supervisor of Mongolia and Tibet.

Article 54: The election supervisors of each Mongolian and Tibetan banner stipulated in the third and fourth paragraphs of Article 31 of the Election Law shall be appointed by the General Election Office from suitable personnel.

Article 55: The election stipulated in the first paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be handled by the General Election Office ordering the Kashag to supervise the election affairs in various parts of Tibet in accordance with the regional election procedures.

Article 56: The election stipulated in the second paragraph of Article 32 of the Election Law shall be handled by the General Election Office appointing suitable personnel as election supervisors to handle all matters related to investigation, registration, and election.

Article 57: Various elections shall be completed within three days.

Article 58: Incumbent provincial, municipal, district, and county-level officials, judicial officials, and military and police chiefs shall not be elected as National Assembly representatives in the electoral districts where they are located.

Article 59: The director, deputy director, general secretary, deputy general secretary, counselors, section chiefs, and staff of the General Election Office shall not be elected as National Assembly representatives. Supervisors and inspectors shall not be elected in the electoral districts under their supervision and inspection. Election supervisors shall not be elected in the regions or groups where they handle elections.

Article 60: The election supervisor shall issue an election notice fifteen days before the election, stating the following: 1. The address of the polling station and ballot counting station; 2. The voting method and date; 3. The number of representatives from the district or group.

Article 61: If a voter has any of the following circumstances, the election supervisor shall order them to leave: 1. Impersonating another person; 2. Causing a disturbance or inciting disobedience on the premises; 3. Carrying a weapon into the premises; 4. Engaging in other improper conduct and refusing to comply with orders.

Article 62: The duties of the polling station officer are as follows: 1. Maintaining order at the polling station; 2. Managing the ballot box, voter register, and voter list; 3. Other matters entrusted by the election supervisor.

Article 63: The duties of the ballot counting station officer are as follows: 1. Maintaining order at the ballot counting station; 2. Counting the number of ballots and calculating the votes received by the candidates; 3. Preserving the ballots; 4. Other matters entrusted by the election supervisor.

Article 64: The polling station supervisor and the ballot counting supervisor shall respectively supervise the voting and ballot counting matters. If the supervisor disagrees with the officer, they shall report to the election supervisor for a decision.

Article 65: After a voter has completed voting, the polling station officer shall stamp the words "Voted" on the citizen certificate and return the original certificate.

Article 66: The ballots and ballot boxes shall be made by the chief election supervisor according to the format in the attached schedule and distributed to the election supervisors, who shall distribute them to the polling station officers before the start of various elections.

Article 67: The polling station officer shall, together with the polling station supervisor, open and inspect the ballot box in public before voting and seal it tightly after inspection.

Article 68: Each election supervisor shall prepare a voter register according to the number of voters in each polling station. The voter register shall state the voter's name, age, ancestral home, and address.

Article 69: The ballots shall be distributed to the polling station, and the polling station officer shall, together with the polling station supervisor, verify the number and seal them tightly. They shall not be unsealed until the voting date, after the seal has been verified in public.

Article 70: After voting is completed, the polling station officer shall, together with the polling station supervisor, immediately seal the ballot box tightly in public. The ballot counting station officer shall, together with the ballot counting supervisor, verify the seal in public before the ballot counting begins, and shall not unseal it. If voters deem it necessary, they may publicly nominate nine to fifteen representatives to prepare seals with their signatures and stamps to seal the ballot box.

Article 71: When preparing Mongolian and Tibetan ballots according to the format, in addition to using Chinese characters, they may be translated and printed on the back of the ballot in the common language of the area.

Article 72: When issuing Mongolian and Tibetan election notices, in addition to using Chinese characters, a translation in the common language of the area may be attached.

Article 73: The polling station officer shall record the following information in the voter register: 1. The name, age, ancestral home, and address of the voter; 2. The polling station and voting date; 3. The number of ballots issued, the number of ballots remaining, and the number of ballots cast.

Article 74: If a voter violates the provisions of Article 61 of these Regulations and is ordered to leave, their ballot shall be collected and noted in the voter register.

Article 75: After voting is completed, the polling station officer shall prepare a report on the voting situation and submit it to the election supervisor together with the remaining ballots, voter register, and voter list. The report shall be countersigned by the polling station supervisor.

Article 76: In the event of a natural disaster or other force majeure event that prevents voting, the polling station officer may report to the election supervisor to reschedule the voting date or location.

Article 77: The voting and ballot counting time shall not be before 8:00 AM or after 6:00 PM. The ballot boxes that have not been voted or counted shall be temporarily locked by the officer and the supervisor and unsealed publicly when voting and ballot counting continue the next day.

Article 78: The election supervisor of each district shall determine the ballot counting time on the day after all ballot boxes have been delivered and announce it in advance. At that time, they shall personally go to the ballot counting station to supervise the ballot counting supervisors and officers in performing their duties.

Article 79: Voters may request an admission ticket from the ballot counting station officer to enter the ballot counting station to observe the ballot counting process, up to the limit of available seats. If necessary, the number of people allowed to enter may be temporarily restricted.

Article 80: When counting ballots, the ballot counting station officer shall, together with the ballot counting supervisor, determine the validity of the ballots. After the determination, it shall be announced publicly.

Article 81: The ballot counting station officer shall prepare a ballot counting record, recording the following information: (1) The total number of ballots cast; (2) The number of invalid ballots; (3) The number of votes received by each candidate.

Article 82: After the ballot counting is completed, the ballot counting station officer shall prepare a report on the ballot counting situation and submit it to the election supervisor together with the ballot counting record, valid ballots, and invalid ballots. The report shall be countersigned by the ballot counting supervisor.

Article 83: Voting records, ballot counting records, and election records shall be made in duplicate for voters or candidates to request access.

Article 84: After the election is completed, the local election supervisor shall prepare a report and submit it to the chief election supervisor, who shall preserve it within the term of office of the current election.

Chapter 6: Invalid Election and Election

Article 85: If an election is invalid and a re-election cannot be held, or if the re-election is still inconclusive, the National Government may designate a candidate.

Article 86: If two or more candidates in the same place have the same name, unless there is another way to prove who should be elected, the election shall be determined by drawing lots.

Article 87: The names of the elected representatives and alternate representatives, as well as the number of votes they received, shall be publicly announced by the chief election supervisor or election supervisor and notified to each elected representative at the same time. After receiving the notice, the elected representative shall indicate in writing within ten days whether or not they are willing to accept the election. If they are unwilling to accept the election, the alternate candidate stipulated in Article 8 of the Election Law shall fill the vacancy in accordance with the law.

Article 88: The election supervisor of each locality shall issue a certificate of election to the elected representatives of each locality, and the style is as shown in the attached schedule. If the election is invalid, the certificate of election, if already issued, shall be ordered to be returned, and the name and the reason for the invalidation shall be announced. Article 89: Each representative shall report to the General Election Office in person five days before the meeting and submit the certificate of election for verification.

Chapter 7: Supplementary Provisions

Article 90: The power of interpretation of these Regulations belongs to the General Election Office.

Article 91: These Regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency, 24th)

National Economic Construction Movement Committee General and Branch Organization Charter Approved by the President and Promulgated Yesterday; Committee Member Candidates Finalized, General Assembly to be Established Soon 26

(Nanjing) The General and Branch Organization Charters of the National Economic Construction Movement Committee have been approved by President Chiang and promulgated on the 24th. The General Assembly charter consists of five chapters and fifteen articles, the Branch Assembly charter consists of five chapters and fourteen articles, and the Sub-branch Assembly charter consists of five chapters and twelve articles. According to Liu Weichi, the Chief Secretary of the General Assembly Preparatory Committee, the General Assembly is expected to be formally established in about a week, and the branch assemblies in various regions can also be organized within two weeks. After the establishment of the General Assembly, a separate department will still be set up. The candidates for the General Assembly committee members have been drafted and submitted to President Chiang for approval, totaling about 300 people. Leaders and experts from all sectors, including economics, commerce, and overseas Chinese, are all being invited, and the list is expected to be announced around the 25th. The first step after establishment will be to provide relief to unemployed youth and train economic construction talents, and an Economic Construction Education Committee will be established to oversee this work. However, in terms of the Economic Construction Movement, the General Assembly will only provide a framework and guidance, while the actual promotion of the work will depend on the efforts and cooperation of the branch assemblies in various regions. The General Assembly will meet once a year, with the first general meeting scheduled for early autumn. It is also reported that the Standing Committee of the General Assembly will likely still be composed of the three preparatory committee members Kong Xiangxi, Wu Dingchang, and Weng Wenhao, with Wu Dingchang serving as the Chairman of the Standing Committee. The main points of the General and Branch Assembly charters are recorded below:

General Assembly Charter: According to Article 2 of the General Charter, it is named the National Economic Construction Movement Committee General Assembly. According to Article 4 of the General Charter, the following staff will be appointed under the President: three to five Standing Committee members, with one designated by the President as the Chairman of the Standing Committee; a number of Committee members; a number of Specialists; one General Secretary; six to twelve Secretaries; and twelve to twenty Clerks. The President has overall responsibility for all assembly affairs. The Standing Committee members are appointed by the President to assist in managing affairs under the President's orders. The Committee members can be divided into several groups to study and discuss various matters separately. The General Secretary is appointed by the President to handle all affairs of the General Assembly. Under the General Secretary, the following sections are established: 1. General Affairs Section; 2. Executive Section; 3. Investigation Section. Specialists and Secretaries are appointed by the President to handle the affairs of each section stipulated in the preceding article. The heads and deputy heads of each section may be concurrently held by Secretaries. The President, Standing Committee members, Committee members, Specialists, General Secretary, Secretaries, and Clerks are all unpaid positions. The General Assembly will meet once a year, and special meetings may be convened when necessary, convened by the President. The expenses of the Assembly will be used frugally from the department's expenses, but if there is not enough in the department's budget, the President will raise the funds.

Branch Assembly Charter: This Branch Assembly, according to Article 2 of the General Charter, is named the National Economic Construction Movement Committee Branch Assembly of a certain province or city. According to Article 4 of the General Charter, the following staff will be appointed under the Branch Assembly President: one General Secretary; a number of Committee members; a number of Specialists; four to six Secretaries; and eight to twelve Clerks. The Branch Assembly President manages all affairs of this Branch Assembly. The Branch Assembly General Secretary is appointed by the Branch Assembly President to assist in managing affairs under the Branch Assembly President's orders. In the absence of the Branch Assembly President, the Branch Assembly General Secretary acts as chairman of the Branch Assembly Committee meeting. The Branch Assembly Committee members can be divided into several groups to study and discuss various matters separately. Under the Branch Assembly General Secretary, the following sections are established: 1. General Affairs Section; 2. Executive Section; 3. Investigation Section. Specialists and Secretaries are appointed by the Branch Assembly President to handle the affairs of each section stipulated in the preceding article. The Branch Assembly President, General Secretary, Committee members, Specialists, Secretaries, and Clerks are all unpaid positions. The Branch Assembly will meet once a year, and special meetings may be convened when necessary, convened by the Branch Assembly President. The resolutions should be reported to the General Assembly at any time. The expenses of the provincial branch assembly will be used frugally from the construction department's expenses, and the expenses of the city branch assembly will be used frugally from the social affairs bureau's expenses. However, if there is not enough in the construction department or social affairs bureau's budget, the Branch Assembly President will raise the funds.

Sub-branch Assembly Charter: The Sub-branch Assembly, according to Article 2 of the General Charter, is named the National Economic Construction Movement Committee Sub-branch Assembly of a certain county or city. According to Article 4 of the General Charter, the following staff will be appointed under the Sub-branch Assembly President: a number of Committee members; a number of Specialists; two to four Secretaries; and four to eight Clerks. The Sub-branch Assembly President manages all affairs of this Sub-branch Assembly. The Sub-branch Assembly Committee members can be divided into several groups to study and discuss various matters separately. The Sub-branch Assembly has the following sections: 1. General Affairs Section; 2. Executive Section. Specialists and Secretaries are appointed by the Sub-branch Assembly President to handle the affairs of the two sections stipulated in the preceding article. The Sub-branch Assembly President, Committee members, Specialists, Secretaries, and Clerks are all unpaid positions. The Sub-branch Assembly will meet twice a year, and special meetings may be convened when necessary, convened by the Sub-branch Assembly President. The resolutions should be reported to the Branch Assembly and then to the General Assembly at any time. The expenses of the county sub-branch assembly will be used frugally from the construction bureau's expenses or the expenses of the organization handling construction matters, and the expenses of the city sub-branch assembly will be used frugally from the expenses of the organization handling construction matters. However, if there is not enough in the construction bureau's or organization's budget, the Sub-branch Assembly President will raise the funds. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) Liu Weichi, Chief Secretary of the National Economic Construction Movement Preparatory Committee, stated that about 300 people have been decided to be appointed as General Assembly committee members. Celebrities and experts from all walks of life have been invited, and many overseas Chinese have also been appointed. The list will be announced after the procedures are completed. The General Assembly is expected to be established next week, and the Assembly will be temporarily located in the ministry. The first general meeting will be held in the cool of autumn. The Standing Committee of the General Assembly will be composed of the three preparatory committee members Wu Dingchang, Kong Xiangxi, and Weng Wenhao, with Wu serving as the Chairman of the Standing Committee. The General Assembly's work plan has also been drafted by the preparatory committee and can be submitted to President Chiang for approval soon. The first focus of the plan is on training construction industry talents, so it is planned to cooperate with the Ministry of Education to provide appropriate training to unemployed youth with considerable talent, and send them to work in various places in the future, so that various undertakings can obtain talent and gradually develop. (Special Dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) The General and Branch Assembly charters of the National Economic Construction Movement Committee have been formulated and promulgated by President Chiang. The General Assembly charter has five chapters and fifteen articles, and the Sub-branch Assembly charter has five chapters and twelve articles. The list of all General Assembly committee members has been supplemented and submitted to President Chiang for approval due to the continued increase in the number of members, and the entire list can be announced within two or three days. The establishment date of the General Assembly has been postponed to next week due to insufficient preparation. It has also been decided to convert the original ministry's reception room into the General Assembly office. Branch assemblies in various provinces and cities such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shaanxi, Jiangxi, Hubei, Anhui, and Chahar provinces, as well as Nanjing and Shanghai, are all being prepared. They can be established separately after the Branch Assembly charters are promulgated. As for the sub-branch assemblies in various counties and cities, they must be carried out after the branch assemblies are established. (Special Dispatch, 24th)

News on National Assembly Preparations 27

(Nanjing) The three types of regulations for the National Assembly election have been passed by the Executive Yuan and can be officially promulgated and implemented soon. The Director and Deputy Director of the Election General Office, Chiang Tso-pin and Chu Min-yi, are actively planning for the early establishment of the office. Issue of Warships Passing Through the Straits - Montreux Conference - Soviet Russia Demands Special Treatment - Black Sea Fleet Should Not Be Restricted by Treaty - France Supports, Japan Opposes, Britain Makes No Statement 28

Montreux, Switzerland The Montreux Conference continued its sessions this morning. The Soviet representative, Foreign Commissar Litvinov, immediately proposed a motion arguing that the maximum tonnage limit set in the new convention draft proposed by Turkey regarding the passage of warships from all countries through the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits should only be applied to "countries not bordering the Black Sea." The provision prohibiting submarines from passing through the straits should also include aircraft carriers, and that warships from Black Sea countries exiting the Black Sea through the straits should not be restricted in the same way as warships from non-Black Sea countries entering the Black Sea through the straits. The Japanese representative, Ambassador to France Sato, immediately expressed disagreement. Japan is prepared to accept the restrictions on warships from all countries entering the Black Sea as stipulated in the new convention draft, but only on the condition that they are applied simultaneously to those exiting the Black Sea. The British representative, Lord Stanhope, Minister of Public Works, refused to participate in the discussion because he had not received instructions from his government. Litvinov then proposed an amendment, arguing that warships of belligerent countries should be prohibited from entering the Black Sea, but this should not apply to those whose purpose is to fulfill obligations under mutual assistance treaties. The meeting was then adjourned and scheduled to continue tomorrow to discuss all commercial clauses contained in the new convention draft by the technical committee this afternoon. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

Montreux, Switzerland Today, at the conference of countries signatory to the Treaty of Lausanne, Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov requested that Soviet warships be given free passage from the Black Sea, so that the Soviet Union could fulfill its obligations under the League of Nations Covenant when necessary. The French representative, Poncet, supported Litvinov's proposal and suggested that the convention should stipulate that all countries may use the straits to fulfill their obligations under regional agreements established within the League of Nations, which would allow France to send warships to aid the Soviet Union in accordance with the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance agreement. (Reuters Dispatch, 21st)

Montreux, Switzerland This afternoon, the Montreux Conference continued its sessions and discussed the issue of the free passage of merchant ships from all countries through the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits, and began to study all the clauses in the new convention draft that could be applied to international commercial interests. According to recent statistics, the total tonnage of ships passing through the two straits each year is 12 million tons, of which Italy accounts for the largest share with 2,527,000 tons, followed by Britain with 1,086,000 tons, followed by Greece, Norway, Romania, Germany, France, and other countries. It is reported that Japan argues that the connection between the new convention on the straits issue and the League of Nations Covenant should be minimized as much as possible. The French representative, former Minister without Portfolio Poncet, met with the Japanese representative, Ambassador to France Sato, today to discuss this matter. Also, at today's meeting, the secretariat received letters from the governments of India and the Union of South Africa, stating that they could not send representatives to attend the meeting, but had no objection to the amendment of the current straits system. The next plenary meeting is scheduled to be held tomorrow. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)

British House of Commons Discusses Foreign Policy - Labor Party Impeachment Motion Rejected - Failure of International Rule of Law Replacing Barbaric Forces - British Politics Still Based on the League of Nations 29

(London) Attlee, leader of the opposition Labor Party, moved an impeachment motion against the government in the House of Commons today, stating that "the British government's decision to pursue a firm and consistent foreign policy has diminished the country's prestige, weakened the League of Nations' position, and endangered peace, and has therefore lost the confidence of this House." Attlee and Sinclair of the opposition Liberal Party both spoke out vehemently against the government's actions. Home Secretary Simon spoke on behalf of the government in response, and Prime Minister Baldwin concluded the debate with a speech. The impeachment motion was then put to a vote and rejected by a vote of 384 to 170.

The atmosphere in the House of Commons today was not as tense as last Thursday when the government announced its intention to support the lifting of sanctions against Italy. Before the meeting, Foreign Secretary Eden had a three-quarter-hour meeting with the King. Italian Ambassador to London Grandi quietly listened to the debate in the audience.

When Attlee moved the impeachment motion, he declared that the government had pursued a weak and hesitant policy over the past five years, causing the country to fall from its high position in 1931 (shouts of ridicule from the cabinet benches). The government abandoned Abyssinia and destroyed the League of Nations, making it no longer an effective tool for seeking peace. Now that Italy is allowed to triumph over Abyssinia, no member of the League of Nations will have any security. The British Empire does not fully agree with the lifting of sanctions, and the most closely affected dominion (the Union of South Africa) strongly opposes this move. What will the natives of South Africa and the world think of this? If Mussolini is willing to expand his rule, will Prime Minister Baldwin fight for the Somaliland Sultanate or the Kenyan war? The government is unwilling to risk peace and has increased the risk of war. The government abandoned the opportunity to unite Europe into a true collective security.

The next speaker was Sinclair, a key member of the Liberal opposition, who said that the government had been consistently controlled by fear during the crisis of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Italy was in the grip of the League of Nations' economic power, and when this weapon was about to take effect, the government abandoned it. The government's policy has allowed the aggressor to profit from outside, and has made the world dependent on dictators. The government should have clearly told Mussolini at the Stresa Conference that if he insisted on his policy towards Abyssinia, the entire British people would rise up against him. Sinclair also did not believe that the League of Nations or sanctions had failed, saying that they had not been given a chance.

Then Simon rose to speak on behalf of the government, saying that he, like all members, deeply felt that the League of Nations had suffered a major setback. Financial and economic sanctions cannot protect a member state from foreign aggression. The effort to replace barbaric power with international order has failed. The government and those who support the government feel no less deeply about the damage this has done to international moralism than the opposition. Some say that sanctions should have been implemented earlier, and they may have been effective today. However, the League of Nations Covenant stipulates that this step cannot be taken until war has broken out. In other words, Eden promoted this action faster than anyone else. Eden had previously stated that Britain was very happy to see the implementation of oil sanctions, but some still blame the British government for the fact that this sanction did not materialize. This is truly an unfair argument. All who hoped that sanctions would have good results are now deeply disappointed to see that sanctions have failed and the Italo-Abyssinian war has ended. The continued implementation of sanctions cannot change this result. Those who implemented sanctions must now decide whether the current environment is right to collude with those who use force to change resolutions. He believes that none of the League of Nations member states are prepared to use this force, and the British government is not prepared to use it either. Some advocate that if Britain goes to war, the British navy in the Mediterranean may be subdued. This is not true. He dares to believe that the British navy would have a very good record in this situation, but the government, in the current European situation and the major dangers surrounding Britain, does not want to see even one ship sunk in a victorious naval battle for the sake of Abyssinia. The government will not change its policy or its loyalty to the League of Nations because of the action it is taking at present. The government is now facing reality and considering how to strengthen the League of Nations' position so that it can cope with this kind of shock and dispute in the future. Serving the League of Nations in this way will be far better than today. The Foreign Secretary has already started this work and has been in contact with other League of Nations member states. This move must also be discussed with the dominions before a decision can be made.

Finally, Prime Minister Baldwin concluded the debate, saying that the government had no intention of condoning Italy's actions. The government has no power to lend money to Italy and does not want to seek this power. Collective security has failed because almost all European countries do not want to carry out military sanctions. The League of Nations' responsibility today is to examine how it can act in the future based on its recent experiences. Britain's policy is still based on the League of Nations.

The Prime Minister then praised Eden for putting his heart into the struggle to maintain the League of Nations, saying that the government's opposition to continuing and strengthening sanctions against Italy is because nothing but military action can slightly change the position of Italy and Abyssinia. The League of Nations has suffered a severe setback, but the failure of the first attempt to implement collective security must not be seen as the death of the League of Nations. When the League of Nations General Assembly meets in September, it will inevitably carry out all matters. At present, the government must not only decide on its own resolutions, but also exchange informal opinions with the governments of the dominion and other member states of the League of Nations, especially France. The second purpose of the government's policy is to pacify the overall situation. Some say that if Britain can secure its own country in the West, the government intends to allow the whole of Europe to seek its own safety. This view is unfounded. However, if the League of Nations ultimately breaks down, then there may be such a day. However, he has all kinds of hopes that when the three major countries start negotiations in the future, they will be able to raise a way to secure the countries of Central Europe, because the British government also hopes to raise it for Britain. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

Oxford University Awards Eden Doctorate of Law 30

(London) Oxford University awarded Foreign Secretary Eden and Oxford University Professor Murray a Doctorate of Law this morning. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

French Government's Foreign Policy: House Votes Confidence; Foreign Minister Delbos Delivers Declaration 31

(Paris) After debating foreign policy today, the House of Representatives, composed of a majority from various countries, jointly proposed a vote of confidence in the government, which passed with a majority of 184 votes. The motion included (1) endorsing the government's declaration and (2) expressing confidence in the government's collective security measures to protect France's peace. Before the vote, Foreign Minister Delbos answered various questions, explaining the government's position, particularly regarding the German threat. Delbos stated that the government's rejection of isolationism or old alliances was a faithful adherence to collective security, and it was deeply aware of the dangers of German aggression. France remains calm and will not accept ambiguous interpretations of violations of the Locarno Pact. It now intends to negotiate a treaty with Mediterranean countries to ensure no hegemony is established in the Mediterranean. He also hopes to establish a compromise in Western Europe to end the crisis that began on March 7 (German troops entering the Rhineland). However, this cannot be achieved solely by France. Italy has informed France of its willingness to cooperate in this effort. France advocates for gradual and universal disarmament under the control of international organizations, while not neglecting the necessary national defenses. France intends to request the convening of an international committee in Geneva to control the production of war materials. To improve the overall economic situation, the French government also intends to request the convening of a committee to study the European unity issue initiated by the late Briand. This committee will include European countries, whether or not they are members of the League of Nations, so that Germany can also participate. Delbos finally mentioned the possibility of peace, stating that if international organizations do not reveal their strength for a long time, France's defense must be maintained at its current level. France has a responsibility to itself and its friends to be in a position to deter all aggression. (Reuter's dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) Following Foreign Minister Delbos's declaration on foreign policy in the parliament, a debate immediately commenced. Several members from the right-wing and center parties successively expressed their opinions, explaining the critical situation in Europe. Among them, Conservative Member of Parliament Grillet stated that Germany now has the immediate capacity to attack Czechoslovakia, for which France has made absolutely no preparations and does not know how to respond. Regarding France itself, "1,800 German tanks, along with several mechanized divisions, could pass through Belgium and reach France within two days. This danger cannot be ignored." Subsequently, Delbos responded, stating that the German Nazi Party advocates racism, and its aspirations are even greater than those who purely advocate nationalism. He is deeply aware of this danger. "However, France remains calm and will do its utmost to safeguard international justice. Germany's abolition of the Locarno Pact should only be regarded as an illegal act, with a clear and unambiguous meaning. When the League of Nations convenes an extraordinary meeting at the end of this month, the signatory countries of the Locarno Pact will naturally take the opportunity to exchange views. If Germany has submitted an answer regarding the British question at that time, France will immediately study it to seek a proper foundation. In short, France does not threaten any country, nor will it allow other countries to threaten it. "France adheres to justice and will do its utmost to complete its arduous task." The discussion concluded at 10 PM. The Senate is scheduled to discuss the government's declaration on Thursday. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

(Paris) Prime Minister Léon Blum attended the Senate this afternoon and delivered a declaration on foreign policy. Foreign Minister Delbos delivered a similar declaration in the House of Representatives. The main points are summarized as follows:

The declaration's first paragraph addresses the collective security mechanism, stating that the League of Nations Covenant should not be subject to sweeping revisions. Only minor textual deletions are needed to clarify the interpretation of the Covenant's articles. In the French government's view, the collective security mechanism should have two key points: (1) All countries neighboring an aggressor must exert their full strength to resist the aggressor. (2) All other member states of the League of Nations must uniformly implement economic and financial sanctions against the aggressor. Regional pacts are neither tools to threaten any country nor do they constitute a pre-World War I alliance system. "The French government now intends to vigorously promote negotiations on regional pacts, such as the Danube Pact and a Mediterranean Pact involving Spain and the Balkan Entente countries." Regarding the German question, the declaration stated that the parties affiliated with the left-wing Popular Front have long sought to reconcile France and Germany and have spared no effort in pursuing this goal. However, Germany's abolition of the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles and its subsequent destruction of the Locarno Pact are still fresh in our minds and cannot be easily forgotten. "Although France is still prepared to consider any German proposals in order to seek a compromise, this compromise should not be directed against any country." Regarding the issue of disarmament, it stated that France has decided to request the League of Nations to establish a permanent committee in Geneva to disseminate as much information as possible regarding the manufacture and control of munitions. The current government should first request the parliament to pass a bill to nationalize the munitions industry, which is the first step in state control. Regarding the Sky Pact, it stated that France is prepared to sign a pact to limit air force armaments, whether in Western Europe or throughout Europe. Finally, the declaration stated that freedom of thought and democratic progress in an environment of peace and freedom are the rights that mankind has inherited from generation to generation, and France is determined to protect them. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) The Senate today passed a bill allowing the Bank of France to lend 10,000,000,000 francs to the government by a vote of 184 to 90. The bill also authorized the government to issue an additional 12,000,000,000 francs in treasury bonds. At the same time, the government's two bills regarding the franc have been announced. One stipulates that anyone who spreads rumors to shake public confidence in the franc and the value of public securities may be sentenced to three months to two years of imprisonment and fined up to 10,000 francs. The other stipulates that anyone who intentionally falsely reports funds held abroad will be fined an amount equal to the amount concealed. The same applies to the concealment of inherited property abroad. The bill to amend the French Bank system has now been submitted to the House of Representatives, stipulating that officials who manage public loans may participate in the bank's new General Affairs Committee, and representatives from industry, commerce, and agriculture may also participate. (Reuter's dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) The government has already ordered the dissolution of various paramilitary organizations and has now ordered the dissolution of the affiliated agencies of these organizations. The "Sons of the Croix-de-Feu," the "Volunteer Corps of the Croix-de-Feu," the "Brigardes" (a group organized by veterans who have experienced long battles), and the "Social Movement Group" will be dissolved by bailiffs, and no incidents have occurred. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

Japanese Foreign Ministry Decides to Strengthen Diplomatic Policy, Focusing on China and Russia 32

(Tokyo) The Foreign Ministry held a meeting at 3:00 PM on the 23rd to determine a new diplomatic policy for overall administrative reform. Foreign Minister Arita, Vice Minister Horiuchi, and all bureau chiefs, directors, and section chiefs attended, and the discussion lasted for three and a half hours. The main points of the decision are as follows:

The international situation centered on Japan is tending to deteriorate, requiring the strengthening of national defense and the establishment of an independent and proactive diplomacy.

Based on the inseparable relationship between Japan and Manchuria, strengthen policies towards Russia and China, while striving to obtain resources and develop trade to establish the people's right to survival.

The Foreign Ministry will prepare a draft based on this outline and submit it to the cabinet meeting on the 10th of next month. To concretely implement this plan, it will improve the various agencies within the Foreign Ministry and increase funding for diplomatic work. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 24th)

(London) The newly appointed Japanese Ambassador, Shigeru Yoshida, arrived here this morning and told the press that Japanese public opinion believes that the friendship between Britain and Japan, whether in the Far East or elsewhere, would be beneficial and necessary if it could be restored and enhanced. This is of great significance, but based on past experience, the sentiments of Britain and Japan regarding the promotion of friendly relations have often failed to occur simultaneously, which is regrettable. In the future, his primary mission will be to stimulate such sentiments so that they appear simultaneously, thereby promoting friendship between the two countries. The first step is to explore and will begin immediately. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 24th)

(London) The new Japanese ambassador, Yoshida, told a Reuters reporter today that Japan is very concerned about the future of Shanghai. Many countries are related to Shanghai, so this has become one of the major issues in the Far East. Yoshida smiled and denied the rumors that he came here with the mission of concluding a British-Japanese agreement, saying that he must first consider the overall situation and then promote mutual understanding based on the traditional friendship between Britain and Japan. When the reporter asked if there was a possibility for Britain and Japan to frankly discuss all unresolved disputes, Yoshida welcomed this view, but said that it contained many disputes, such as the interests of Britain and Japan in China and the future of China, Japan's trade in British colonies, and naval construction issues, which are not easy to resolve. As commercially focused countries like Britain and Japan are bound to have conflicts on many points, it is not easy to see both countries willing to discuss the same issue at the same time. However, he felt that Britain and Japan must eventually reach a compromise, and the peace and prosperity of the Far East depend on this compromise. Yoshida did not want to discuss the issue of smuggling in North China because Japan's point of view has not been properly heard. Japan Uses Trade Protection Act to Boycott Australian Specialties 34

(Nanjing) The government, due to the Australian government's increase in tariffs, decided to invoke the Trade Protection Act as a retaliatory measure. The relevant ministerial order has been approved, and preparations for the order and other matters have been completed. Therefore, it is scheduled to invoke the Act on the 25th, effective immediately. The intention has been telegraphed to Murai, the Consul-General in Sydney, to notify the Australian government. The Act adopts an import license system for wool, wool waste, or old wool, wheat, and wheat flour, but adopts an export license system for wool waste and wool rags. Tariffs on cheese, condensed milk, and butter will be increased by 50%. As for the aforementioned import or export license system, the implementation procedures will be announced by the Ministry of Commerce and Industry in a ministerial order, and the Minister of Commerce and Industry will issue a notice to wool importers, instructing them to report the actual imports, the actual use, and the storage quantities of wool to wool industrialists and others for record-keeping. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 24th)

International Anti-Narcotics Conference Passes Draft Convention Punishing Illegal Trafficking 35

(Geneva) The international conference on drafting a "Convention for the Punishment of Illegal Trafficking in Narcotics" recently passed the draft convention by a vote of thirteen to one. "Contracting States, wherever they enjoy extraterritorial jurisdiction in the territory of another Contracting State, and their people illegally traffic in narcotics within that country, and the courts of that country cannot prosecute them in accordance with the various punitive measures contained in this Convention, hereby agree to enact necessary laws so that the consular courts stationed in that country may prosecute the drug traffickers in accordance with the law, at least the same as those who commit crimes in their own country." The Chinese representative, Hu Shih-tse, the country's minister to Switzerland, declared that once this principle is adopted, it will greatly facilitate China's anti-drug movement. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

International Labor Conference Discusses Workers' Vacation Bill 36

(Geneva) The International Labor Conference recently discussed the issue of workers' annual leave and passed a draft international convention by a vote of 95 to 16, advocating for one week of annual leave with full pay. According to the draft convention, it must be passed by a two-thirds majority to be established. The results of today's vote did not reach the required number of votes, so the conference will hold a second vote tomorrow. It is generally expected that it will be confirmed and passed at that time. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

(Geneva) The International Labor Conference rejected this morning a proposal to implement a 40-hour work week in the construction and steel industries. The French labor representative, Challier, delivered a speech expressing disappointment, stating, "The reduction of working hours is inevitable. This is not due to human volition, but the natural result of mechanical development. Whether you agree or not, if you do not accept it voluntarily, you will eventually be forced to accept it." He also said that France is now implementing labor and social laws (i.e., the 40-hour work week proposal). If other countries do not reduce working hours, France's economy will be threatened and will have to find ways to protect it. The Belgian labor representative, Meldon, spoke after Challier, with similar wording. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

US Democratic Party Convention Decides to Fight Republicans with the New Deal; Roosevelt is Strongly Supported by Representatives; Union Leader Assists in Drafting Platform 40

Philadelphia, USA The Democratic National Convention opened here today at 1:02 PM. This is the first time since 1920 that the party has been on the defensive. The delegates attending the meeting are eager to answer the Republican attacks on the New Deal, so the issues of the party's platform and the conservative defectors have become secondary. The opening of the conference began with a prayer by Bishop Lamb, followed by a speech by Postmaster General Farley, chairman of the National Committee, unconditionally accepting the Republican challenge and making the New Deal the focus of the election campaign. Farley said, "The current problem of the people is beyond doubt: should we continue the New Deal that is saving the people from fire and water, or should we return the power to the old guys who destroyed the government before?" Farley attributed the responsibility for the economic downturn entirely to the Republican Party, saying that the financial giants were the backbone of the recent Republican governments. In 1933, they had fallen into an irrecoverable situation. After receiving the assistance of President Roosevelt, they were able to get rich again and deliberately slandered in order to destroy the people's faith in the president. As for the Republican Party's platform, it is a hodgepodge, trying to cover up the true face of the conservatives with the mask of liberalism. The reason why their candidate, Landon, was nominated was because he was able to meet the conditions of the big capitalists in the East and tried his best to express his liberal attitude in the West. When Farley mentioned President Roosevelt in his speech, the delegates cheered loudly. After the speech, the representatives paraded along the meeting place, each holding the flag of their state, which was similar to the scene when Hollywood made crowd films. Secretary of State Hull, New York Governor Lehman, and other nationally known figures also participated. The meeting adjourned at 2:38 PM. (National News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Philadelphia, USA The Democratic National Convention opened here at noon today. Postmaster General Farley, chairman of the Democratic National Committee, first gave a speech, which was broadcast nationwide by radio. Farley declared in his speech that to remove all smoke screens, the point of contention today is whether the new measures to save the country from disaster and depression should continue to be implemented, or should the government return to the hands of the general "old businessmen" who destroyed it before. The Republican Party's election platform is full of stale talk and empty declarations. The wealthy are now squandering millions of dollars in order to restore the ambiguous era that made some people rich. This generation eventually brought the country to the brink of bankruptcy. At the end of Farley's speech, he predicted that the real new measures would continue in a fair and orderly manner under the leadership of a quiet, capable, and brave leader, Roosevelt. After Farley's speech, the conference was extended to the evening. The evening meeting began with a speech by Senator Barkley, who made a "centrist" speech criticizing the US Supreme Court for destroying many of President Roosevelt's New Deal orders, saying that the majority of the "nine old men" had made "painful questions" about the Constitution in their resolutions. Barkley then criticized the financial outline of the administrative procedures set by Republican presidential candidate Landon, but Barkley made a statement to be refuted later regarding Hoover's criticism that the New Deal damaged American freedom. Barkley said that behind Hoover's call for freedom are the unforgettable pawnbrokers in the Republican Party, the real estate companies in the Republican Party, namely the American Liberty League, and the various figures who plot to squeeze the blood and flesh of the ox, namely securities traders and privileged people. He also said that President Roosevelt had rejected the suggestion that he should exercise dictatorial power. President Roosevelt is the epitome of justice. (Reuter's dispatch, 23rd)

Philadelphia, USA It is heard that the first draft of the Democratic Party's platform cannot suppress the hopes of the party's leaders. Senator Lenores is now trying to add a clause to the party's platform to prohibit all immigrants from entering the country until the number of unemployed people is reduced. Lewis, the president of the Miners Union, is regarded by the union as the first labor president of the United States in the future. He has been invited to assist in drafting the labor relations party's platform. Sasaki Death Case: British Legation Opens Trial Yesterday 44

(Peiping) British Consul Fitzmaurice opened a coroner's court this morning at the British Embassy to investigate the death of Japanese officer Sasaki. British soldiers Kirk, Barrieu, and Hunter, who were involved in the disturbance in a drinking establishment on the night of May 26, the night Sasaki died, were summoned for questioning. Royal Counsel Mr. Buller-Fullerton-Smith served as the prosecutor, and Tianjin lawyer Kander represented the defendant. Mr. Buller-Fullerton-Smith stated that the summonses issued to the defendants were too vague because they would be asked to testify, and the summonses should clearly state that bodily harm was inflicted on a Japanese person (and that Sasaki was killed). Mr. Buller-Fullerton-Smith briefly outlined the reasons for the prosecution, saying that on the night of May 26, Kirk and Hunter had beaten several times in a disreputable establishment run by Koreans, but there was no evidence of Barrieu's guilt, so he was released immediately. Mr. Buller-Fullerton-Smith continued that the beating became acute after midnight, at which time Sasaki, a Japanese man who had arrived in Peiping for vacation on May 26, and a companion had just left the Kinzawa (transliteration) café on Hada Men Street when they saw two British soldiers arguing with a rickshaw puller. They stopped to watch, but unexpectedly, the British soldiers started beating Sasaki. Sasaki's companion fled to his hotel, but Sasaki did not follow. When the companion returned, he found Sasaki lying on the ground unconscious. He was sent to a hospital, where a doctor said he had died. Sasaki had been hit above his right eye, fracturing his skull and causing death from internal bleeding. A piece of torn cloth was found next to Sasaki's body, proving that he had been beaten by British soldiers. Next, Japanese man Oonishi, who arrived in Peiping from Shenyang on May 26, testified that on that night, he had gone to a Korean drinking establishment. Before midnight, he and a Japanese waitress were sitting in a room behind the drinking establishment when two foreign soldiers of unknown nationality broke in. One of them raised his fist and struck him heavily above the right eye, leaving a wound about one inch long. The soldier then hit him again, but he could no longer recognize the two soldiers. Many Japanese, Korean, and Chinese people came to court to testify in this case. Because the testimony had to be translated into English, the trial could not be concluded quickly, and it will take about two weeks to finish. (Reuters, 24th)

(Peiping) The British consular trial of the British soldier's killing of Sasaki was held at 11:30 this morning at the British Embassy under the presidency of Consul Fitzmaurice. British lawyers and Japanese witnesses were present. Based on a map submitted by the Japanese Embassy, the incident, the route taken by the British soldiers that night to the Korean drinking establishment until the killing of Sasaki, was made into a Japanese version of the certificate. A recess was taken at 12:30, and the trial resumed at 2:30. (Domei, 24th)
