Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Actively Preparing for Children's Savings 121

Savings Account Book Set at One Yuan Per Account; Scheduled to Begin Next Month and Publicize in Various Regions

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, in order to foster the virtue of thrift in children, is launching a children's savings program. Various measures have been approved by the Ministry of Communications and are now being actively prepared. It is scheduled to be implemented next month. Details are as follows:

Savings Measures The first clause of the children's savings program states that the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications will handle children's savings in accordance with these measures in order to foster the virtue of thrift in children. The second clause states that savings under this program are limited to passbook savings. The third clause states that all postal savings institutions in various regions will handle this type of savings and may first conduct pilot programs with enrolled children. The fourth clause states that children under the age of twenty may deposit savings in accordance with the provisions of this program. Those who wish to deposit savings according to ordinary passbook savings may do so. The fifth clause states that savings deposits are based on the savings passbook, and withdrawals are based on the seal. The savings passbook will be specially stamped with the words "Children's Savings Account" for identification purposes. The sixth clause states that each time a savings depositor deposits savings, it must be a minimum of one yuan. If it is less than one yuan, they may collect savings grid paper and purchase and paste savings stamps, or collect savings bags and deposit the money until it reaches one yuan, then deposit it. The seventh clause states that savings deposits may not exceed 20 yuan per household per month, and the total amount may not exceed 200 yuan. The eighth clause states that savings withdrawals may not exceed twice a month, and each time may not exceed one-fifth of the savings deposit. If the account has been opened for less than six months, the savings deposit may not be withdrawn to close the account. The ninth clause states that the savings interest rate is increased by half a percent compared to ordinary passbook savings, calculated at a weekly rate of 0.5%. The tenth clause states that the savings stamps will be the current five-cent and ten-cent stamps. If the postal savings institution deems it necessary, it may print two types of one-cent or two-cent stamps. The eleventh clause states that in addition to preparing savings grid paper, postal savings institutions will also prepare savings bags to be distributed to savings account holders. The twelfth clause states that other matters are subject to the provisions of postal savings laws and regulations. The thirteenth clause states that these measures will be implemented from the date of approval by the Ministry of Communications.

Implementation Matters 　Request the Ministry of Communications to forward to the Executive Yuan, ordering the Ministry of Education to instruct educational institutions in various regions to promote children's savings; Postal savings institutions in various regions will send personnel to various schools to clarify the significance of children's savings and devote themselves to the following points: (A) Lecture on the virtue of thrift in various primary and secondary schools to encourage students' interest in saving; (B) Print savings publicity leaflets and distribute them to students for reading; (C) Draw savings publicity patterns and distribute them to primary and secondary schools for posting for public viewing; (D) Print savings deposit and withdrawal brochures so that students can understand the savings procedures; Send personnel to various schools on a regular basis to collect savings deposits and open accounts, and distribute savings grid paper and savings bags; Entrust various schools to sell savings stamps; The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will prepare savings publicity cups, divided into A, B, and C levels. Each time child savings account applicants are solicited, the cup for the most new accounts will be given to the child with the most accounts in that area, with prizes for the second and third tier categories, so as to encourage new account establishment;

Scheduled Establishment After the children's savings measures of the local Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau have been approved by the Ministry of Communications, the Bureau is now engaged in internal organization and actively planning various implementation procedures. According to sources in the Savings Department, the savings program is scheduled to be implemented next month. At that time, personnel will be dispatched to various primary and secondary schools to promote it.

Refusing to Accept the Smoking Sentence: Gu Zhuxuan's Appeal Case Concluded; Jia Furong and Wu Lu's Appeal Case Simultaneously Heard; All Three Defendants Strenuously Attempted to Shirk Responsibility for the Charges Against Them; Sentencing Set for 2:00 PM on the 26th 122

In the case of the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, a Ningbo native and former manager of the Great World amusement park, the instigator, Gu Zhuxuan, was arrested by the police department of the Special Second Court and sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment and ten years of deprivation of civil rights. Gu, refusing to accept the verdict, filed an appeal with the Third Branch of the High Court. While detained in the foreign disease ward attached to the Guangci Hospital within the detention center, he instigated fellow inmates Zhao Guangfu, Zhang Tinggui, and others to commit perjury and retract their confessions, hoping to escape the death penalty. The High Court discovered this and suspended the trial, referring the newly discovered perjury case to the Prosecutor's Office of the Special Second Court for investigation and prosecution according to law. The investigation is still ongoing. While in the foreign disease ward, Gu also committed the offense of bribing the warden to obtain opium for smoking. This was reported by inmate Wang A'er and others. The Prosecutor's Office of the Special Second Court investigated and prosecuted the warden, Jia Furong, and Wu Lu, for dereliction of duty. Regarding Gu Zhuxuan's smoking, the police department prosecuted him in the Special Second Court. Although Gu denied smoking during the trial and no evidence of opium addiction was found by the forensic doctor, the presiding judge, based on the confiscated evidence of opium pipes and smoking paraphernalia, as well as the accusers' statements, sentenced Gu to eight months of imprisonment. Jia, Wu, and Gu, all three defendants, refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court in accordance with the law. The Third Branch of the High Court had already concluded the trial of Gu Zhuxuan and Wang Xinggao's murder appeal case on the 20th of this month, both in the morning and afternoon, and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 PM on the 26th (the day after tomorrow). Details have been published in this newspaper. The appeal case concerning Jia, Wu, and Gu's dereliction of duty and opium-related charges was scheduled for trial yesterday afternoon. The High Court and the police department, considering the gravity of Gu's case, notified the judicial police chief to dispatch detectives to ensure security. At three chimes of the bell, Zhu Huanbiao, acting president of the Third Branch of the High Court, along with Judges Shi and Liao, and Prosecutor Dong Qiming, arrived at the Third Criminal Court for the trial. Gu Shouxi, representing the police department, and the defense lawyers selected by the appellants, appeared in court on time. The court ordered Gu Zhuxuan, Jia Furong, and Wu Lu to be brought to the court. After questioning their ages, professions, and addresses, the court announced that for the convenience of the trial, Gu Zhuxuan's opium smoking case and Jia Furong and Wu Lu's dereliction of duty case would be combined. The court ordered the bailiffs to take Jia and Wu down first and then asked Gu Zhuxuan to state his reasons for appeal. Gu claimed, "While detained in the foreign disease ward, I did not smoke. I used to socialize outside and became addicted to smoking at the age of thirty-eight. But while I was sick, I didn't want to smoke anymore. I was arrested and fell ill five days after being released from the hospital. The doctor told me to take Puzi Lingwan pills, and then the Guangci Hospital gave me white powder." When asked what illness he had when he was transferred back from the foreign disease ward to the prison, he answered, "My stomach was bloated and uncomfortable. I was afraid my old addiction was acting up, so Dr. Hu gave me medicine to drink." When asked, "On June 1st, this court received a report from the acting warden and the warden's office, stating that the medical officer examined you and found that your muscles and bones ached and your legs and feet were uncomfortable at night. When questioned, you replied that you had been smoking for three years, and it was the addiction acting up," he answered, "I was taking medicine powder every day in the foreign disease ward. After being transferred to the prison, I didn't take it, so I fell ill." The judge instructed Gu, "You have a reputation and personality in the business world. Why are you unwilling to admit it in this court? Are you afraid of implicating Jia and Wu?" Gu replied, "No, I did smoke when I was outside. I haven't smoked since I was in the detention center, and I'm not trying to cover it up." The judge further instructed, "The government is now banning smoking and drugs, and it is allowing smokers to reform and quit. Since you were addicted, why didn't you honestly report it and quit, instead of taking substitute drugs? If you had quit, you would have been detoxified long ago, considering how long you have been in custody." He also asked about the four opium pipes and a bamboo tube found by Section Chief Ouyang Sen in the disease ward on December 24th last year, and that the forensic doctor proved that the bamboo tube contained opium residue. Gu replied, "They were not found on my person or in my bed. I don't know where they were found." When asked, "Did you order Wu Lu to buy opium for you and give him five yuan? Each yuan could buy four pieces of opium," Gu answered, "No." When asked, "Did your nanny bring you food one day and say that opium was also inside? Warden Jia was also nearby when she said this," Gu answered, "No. When things were brought from home, detectives and Annamite constables were watching by the side." At this point, Jia Furong was brought to the court and ordered to state his reasons for appeal. Jia claimed that he refused to accept the five-year sentence for dereliction of duty for covering up smoking. He said that Section Chief Ouyang Sen found the opium pipes based on Wang A'er's report. Wang was digging a hole to escape, and Warden Duan discovered it. After questioning Wang, he learned that the foreign disease ward contained prisoners, wardens, and constables, making it very complicated. "I only oversee and watch over prisoners to prevent fights or escapes. I don't know who the opium pipes belonged to. Only the mothers can enter the ward three times a day to deliver tea and water. Guo Shanyu and Li Heshang extorted and argued with Gu Zhuxuan. I stopped them and they resented me and accused me. Liu Mingjing's fingers were also yellow because he smoked cigarettes for him. I saw it and reprimanded him, and he also resented me and accused me of covering up smoking. When family members deliver things to prisoners, they can only reach the first iron gate. After inspection, they can be delivered inside. The inspection cannot be concealed under the eyes of detectives and constables. I did not use soap to make a key to open the small room door and let Gu smoke. The bamboo tube that was found also did not have a pipe bowl. Wang A'er took the bamboo tube out from the toilet. This evidence is not complete. I ask for a clear judgment." When asked why Gu did not show signs of withdrawal for a long time in the foreign disease ward, but showed signs of withdrawal two days after being transferred back to the prison, suggesting that Gu smoked in the disease ward, Jia replied, "I have been away from the disease ward for three or four months. I don't know." Then, Wu Lu was brought to the court and ordered to state his reasons for appeal. Wu claimed, "Because inmate Wang A'er attempted to escape and was brought back, he said he stole opium pipes. The section chief's report based on his report is untrue. I serve in the foreign disease ward, but I don't enter the wards. I only inspect the things brought by the prisoners' family members. I inspect in front of the constables assigned by the police station. I did not see any prisoners smoking in the ward, and I did not buy opium for Gu and deliver it through the window. If I had done such a thing and evidence was found, the warden would have notified my chief and punished me. But at that time, it was not mentioned that I was involved. I was detained two months later. It's really unfair." At this point, the court ordered Wang A'er, prisoner number 133, to testify. He said that he lived in the same ward as Gu Zhuxuan and saw Gu smoking in the small room twice a day, after lunch and dinner. He also saw Gu give money to Warden Wu to buy opium, and Wu gave Gu tin foil packages through the window twice. The court then repeatedly questioned the three appellants and Wang A'er, and then considered that the investigation was over and the facts were clear. It ordered the opening of arguments. First, the prosecutor presented his opinion on the two cases, followed by the police department's lawyer and Gu Zhuxuan's defense lawyer arguing. Then, Li and Gao, the lawyers for Jia and Wu, argued. The court declared the arguments in the two cases closed and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 PM on the 26th. The appellants were remanded to custody separately. The court adjourned at almost eight chimes of the bell.

Selling Poison Pills for Profit; Husband and Wife Both Imprisoned; Each Sentenced to Seven Years 128

Ye Yuxi, a Chinese detective of the Jiaxing Road Police Station, and detective Dong Qingquan, learned that someone was selling the drug "red pills" for profit at No. 304 of the same road. They sent an informant with a "double-corner" coin with a secret mark to purchase the pills. The purchase was confirmed. At 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, they secretly went with a Western detective to the address and arrested Jie Yuquan, a native of Taixing. They also saw his wife, Ji, lying idle in bed, with a set of red pills, a pipe, and a lamp nearby, about to take the pills. They confiscated three large bags and twelve small bags of red pills, totaling 1,830 pills, as well as 96 empty red pill bags, banknotes, corner tickets, and copper coins totaling more than six yuan, and a large bamboo tube. Upon questioning, it was stated that the red pills were purchased from Zhao Yuan, a woman at No. 60, Lane 166, East Jiaxing Road. The detectives escorted Ji to arrest her, but she suddenly changed her statement, saying that it was not this woman, but Chen Zhou, an old woman from Haiyan who worked at the cigarette paper shop at No. 247, Oujia Road. They went to arrest the old woman, but no red pills were found. They took everyone to the police station and detained them separately. Yesterday morning, Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Municipal Council, described the case in detail to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court and requested an investigation. The Chinese and Western detectives then reported the details of the case and presented the evidence. Upon questioning Jie Yuquan, his testimony was evasive. Jie Ji admitted to taking the pills for medical reasons. Chen Zhou claimed that she was a servant in the cigarette paper shop, was 65 years old, and would not dare to commit such an illegal act. She said that Jie Ji was falsely accusing her and asked for judgment. Judge Xiao Xiefen sentenced Jie Yuquan and Jie Ji to seven years of imprisonment each. The evidence was confiscated, and Chen Zhou was released.

Regulations on the Inspection of Imported Goods for Transportation and Sales; The Two Railway Bureaus Received Orders from the Ministry to Notify the Transportation Department 129

The Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Administrations received a written order from the Ministry of Railways stating that the Ministry of Finance had consulted and found that the "Provisional Regulations on the Inspection of Imported Goods for Transportation and Sales" had been promulgated by the Executive Yuan and distributed. Now, in accordance with these regulations, the following provisions are separately stipulated: In accordance with the provisions of Article 1, Paragraph 2 of the regulations, the types of goods that should be inspected are rayon, alcohol, alcoholic beverages, whiskey, brandy, Japanese sake, scented wine, Du Gong's shochu, various sweet wines, aniline dyes, rubber boots, rubber shoes, rubber tires, canned food, cigarettes, paper, rouge, perfume, electrical materials, dry batteries, kerosene, diesel oil, various piece goods, dried scallops, various dried seafood, caustic soda, and sugar. In accordance with Article 9 of the regulations, the design of the transportation and sales license and the distribution license is stipulated. The transportation and sales license shall be printed and prepared by the Customs. (The distribution license shall be printed and prepared by the trade association, chamber of commerce, or factory union, and a handling fee may be charged, not exceeding five cents in national currency per sheet.) In accordance with Article 10 of the regulations, the method of obtaining a license is stipulated (with attached application form, certificate form, and license form). The designated agency has been stipulated in the licensing method. The Ministry has sent copies of the license forms, licensing methods, application form, and certificate form for review, and ordered that the original documents be copied and issued for notification and transfer to the subordinate authorities for unified notification. The bureau has transferred the order to the Transportation Department for notification.

The Public Security and Health Bureaus Regularly Inspect Public Places; A Notice to Restaurants to Pay Attention to Summer Hygiene 132

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security and Health Bureaus jointly issued a notice to citizens, stating that since the "Restaurant Management Regulations" were promulgated in the city, many have faithfully followed them, but some have not fully complied. As summer has arrived, all restaurants should pay close attention to hygiene in order to prevent epidemics. The most important points of the regulations are listed below for compliance. Those who deliberately violate them will be strictly investigated and punished. In addition to ordering the subordinates to conduct inspections of each store, a special notice is issued for general information. The main rules are: Do not sell stale food. Food must be covered with gauze to prevent flies and gnats. Bowls, chopsticks, and utensils must be boiled and wiped clean. Toilets must be clean and should use disinfectant, and must be far away from the kitchen. Do not hire those with infectious diseases as employees. In addition to distributing the above articles and notices by area on the next two days, it was also decided to conduct inspections of public places between the 27th and 28th. According to the person in charge of the Health Bureau, the inspection procedures are currently being coordinated with the Public Security Bureau. The standards have also been set, which can be roughly divided into three categories: Whether the building is dangerous and whether the sunlight and air are flowing, whether the facilities are clean and whether the goods are domestic, and whether the personnel employed are neat, clean, and polite. It is reported that the inspectors will be composed of health inspectors, police officers, boy scouts, and security corps, and will be directed by the Youth Service Corps. The inspection should be conducted in a way that does not hinder normal business operations. For example, theaters and bathhouses should be inspected in the morning.

Kang Xiangrong, Purchasing Agent of Reqi Foreign Firm, Accused of Abandonment by Concubine 133

Plaintiff Hospitalized, Seeking Over 40,000 Yuan in Medical Expenses

Kang Xiangrong, a hardware and medicine purchasing agent for Reqi Foreign Firm on Reqi Road, has worked at the firm for many years and accumulated considerable wealth. Recently, a Ningbo woman named Kang Shi Jinying (age 30), residing at No. 52, Dazhong Lane, Tongfu Road, engaged lawyer Li Baosen to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, accusing him of abandonment and requesting a judgment ordering him to pay for living expenses and medical care, totaling

National currency of 43,200 yuan. The case was heard by Judge Huang Risheng in Criminal Court No. 8 at 10:30 a.m. yesterday. The defendant Kang Xiangrong did not appear, but engaged lawyer Li Fengshen to appear in court. Lawyer Li Bao, representing the plaintiff, stated that the plaintiff, Kang Shi Jinying, is currently suffering from severe lung disease with swelling of the throat and a critical condition, and is hospitalized in Room 7 of the Chinese Red Cross Hospital, fearing she will soon pass away. Therefore, she could not appear in person today. The lawyer also presented

The intention of the lawsuit, stating that the plaintiff and defendant Kang Xiangrong began cohabitating five years ago, when Shi was only twenty-six. The defendant falsely claimed to be unmarried and willing to take her as his wife, vowing to grow old together. They cohabitated at No. 5, Dazhong Lane, Tongfu Road. For several years, they made countless vows and were extremely affectionate. All household expenses were fully borne by the defendant. Last summer, Shi suddenly fell ill with lung disease and was vomiting blood. The defendant sent her to the Hongqiao Sanatorium for

Three months of treatment, from which she recovered. The medical expenses were also paid by the defendant. Recently, because the plaintiff's lung disease recurred, the defendant immediately became abusive, not only cutting off financial support but also ceasing to visit. The plaintiff suffered greatly from the shock, and her condition worsened accordingly. Attempts to negotiate were unsuccessful. The plaintiff is now hospitalized in the Red Cross Hospital with no funds for medical expenses. Her condition is deteriorating daily, her throat is swollen, she cannot eat, and she is in critical condition. According to the doctor, she will soon pass away. The defendant's behavior clearly

Violates Article 294 of the Criminal Law regarding the crime of malicious abandonment. The lawsuit also includes a civil request for living expenses and medical treatment, at a minimum of 500 yuan per month, for a period of one and a half years, totaling 9,000 yuan. In addition, future living expenses, according to previous payment practice, should be 100 yuan per month, calculated for twenty-eight and a half years, totaling 24,200 yuan, for a combined total of 43,200 yuan. Furthermore, the plaintiff is terminally ill and should be questioned at the hospital. Defendant's defending lawyer Li Fengshen stated that the plaintiff had previously

Filed a lawsuit with your court based on the same facts, which was rejected. Filing a lawsuit again seems procedurally inappropriate. According to criminal law, a case cannot be brought twice and should be dismissed. Furthermore, the purpose of the lawsuit is purely for money. In reality, the plaintiff abandoned the defendant because the defendant repeatedly asked her to return home and cohabitate, but she refused. Last year, the plaintiff was ill and stayed in a special ward in the sanatorium. The medical expenses amounted to over 2,700 yuan after three months of treatment, which can be considered extremely wasteful. Judge Huang ordered the lawyers of both parties to start the debate on the procedure first, and announced that the verdict would be announced on a later date.

British Shanghai Public Omnibus Company, Thirteenth Annual Shareholders' Meeting 136

Slight Profit Remaining After Interest and Other Expenses, Approximately One Accident per 1.4 Million Miles

The British Shanghai Public Omnibus Company held its thirteenth annual shareholders' meeting at the Sassoon Company, the general manager's office, on Monday. Chairman Arnold presided. The shareholders present represented 145,100 shares. In his report on the company's operations and business conditions during the year, the chairman stated that in 1935, the total number of seats on all the company's buses was 6,127, compared to 5,276 in 1934. Although the number of seats had increased, the total number of passengers had decreased, indicating that the crowding was not as severe as before. According to the average mileage driven, each seat could accommodate 50 passengers per day, so the company's entire fleet could carry 300,000 passengers per day. However, the actual number of passengers carried daily was only about 100,000. At the end of last year, the company had a total of 166 buses, of which 131 were recently manufactured and equipped with diesel oil engines. These new buses accounted for 88% of the net value of the fleet at the end of last year. In 1935, the company's buses traveled a total of 5,148,690 miles, with a serious accident occurring on average every 1,391,50 miles. The year's income, after deducting interest, directors' fees, auditor's fees, and depreciation, left a net profit of 26,568 yuan. After deducting this amount, the company still owed 67,201 yuan at the end of last year, which has been rolled into the 1936 accounts. The profit for 1935 was less than that for 1934, mainly due to changes in the company's depreciation rules and the low value of copper coins. The decrease in passengers by approximately one million also reduced revenue by 18,253 yuan. Fares are still calculated based on copper coins, with 300 coins valued at one yuan. If this rate can be maintained, the income for 1936 will be more substantial. The meeting then unanimously approved the 1935 accounts and elected new directors and auditors before adjourning.

Setting Up a Lighthouse on Yingyou Mountain Island 145

Customs General Taxation Department, Maritime Affairs Section, Notice No. 1085: It has been determined that a lighthouse should be set up on Yingyou Mountain Island in Lianyungang Port in Haizhou Bay, under the jurisdiction of the Donghai Customs, to facilitate navigation. The details of the setup and date are provided below for the information of all merchants. This notice includes: 1. Lighthouse Location: The lighthouse is located near the easternmost tip of Yingyou Mountain Island, approximately 119 degrees 33 minutes east longitude and 34 degrees 43 minutes north latitude. Its position is approximately 128 feet above the high tide level. 2. Lighthouse Details: The lighthouse is an unmanned lighthouse equipped with a sixth-order white flashing light. It emits a white flash every three seconds, with a light duration of one-tenth of a second and a dark duration of two and seven-tenths seconds. 3. Lighthouse Range: The light can be seen within 12 nautical miles on a clear day. However, it is blocked by Yingyou Mountain Island approximately between 210 degrees and 62 degrees north. 4. Installation Date: Around June 27 of this year, with no further notice issued at that time. 5. Related Charts: British Admiralty Chart No. 3480. June 19, Republic of China Year 25. Karnell, Surveying Officer, Maritime Affairs Section.

Letters to the Editor 150

Dear Editor, I have read the "Shanghai News" section of your newspaper on June 15, which reported on "Shen Aizhen and Lin Xingyuan's divorce suit, citing gonorrhea as the reason." One part of the article stated: "The official said to Lin Xingyuan, 'According to the forensic doctor's report, you definitely have gonorrhea.' Lin replied, 'I have chronic gonorrhea, but it can be cured. I ask for your understanding.'" Although Xingyuan went to the forensic doctor's office for examination that day, he was not examined because the forensic doctor's office did not have the necessary instruments. On that day, Xingyuan also did not admit in court that he had gonorrhea. I am afraid that this is inaccurate hearsay, which is very relevant to Xingyuan's reputation. I am therefore writing to request a correction. I respectfully wish you good health. Sincerely, Lin Xingyuan, June 22.

Dear Editor, This is according to what the person concerned, Fei Jinlai, said, I saw in the "Shanghai News" section of Shen Bao, a section that reported that I, Fei Jinlai, had sexually assaulted a young girl, after looking at it, I was horrified, I am afraid that the report in your newspaper is not at all correct. The reasons are that I, Fei Jinlai, am working in the Jingyi Wood Factory, and the factory found earlier that a worker was mixing wood into scrap materials, which was stolen and transported out of the factory. It was learned that this was related to Gao Guangzhou and other workers in the factory. The factory authorities ordered that I, Fei Jinlai, go to Gao Guangzhou's house the next day for investigation. In the end, I, Fei Jinlai, found that the material used for burning in Gao Guangzhou's house was the same as the material from the Jingyi Factory, so I got into an argument with Gao Guangzhou, so Gao was anxious for a while and twisted me around and struck myself with a glass, and reported that I, Fei Jinlai, first beat him etc. Fortunately, the Public Security Bureau found out the truth and released me. Because this matter concerns my personal reputation, please request a correction according to the law, as a public service. Best regards, Shanghai Shen Bao, Lawyer Liu Shifang, June 24.

Shanghai's Oil Extraction Industry 152

— Edited by China Credit

(Twenty-Ninth in the Series of Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Overviews)

I. Overview: Using plant seeds (mainly rapeseed, cottonseed, sunflower seeds, soybeans, etc.) to make oil cakes and extract the oil content has a long history in our country, but all production is done by hand and the scale is very small. Since the British Taikoo Foreign Firm established a modern oil extraction plant in Yingkou, Northeast China, in the 21st year of Guangxu, the industry in China began to take a new stage. Shanghai was the first city in China to be baptized by modern enterprises, so the Dadde Machine Oil Extraction Plant rose the following year. The plant was funded by Sheng Xuanhuai and managed by Zhu Zhiyao, specializing in the production of cottonseed oil and cottonseed cake. Afterwards, as far as Shanghai is concerned, there were quite a few new-style oil extraction industries that followed, such as the Huashang Dasheng, Lide, Tongchang, Dayou, and Yangshang Zengyu factories, all of which were founded during the Guangxu period. At that time, on the one hand, there were few domestic competitors, and on the other hand, neighboring Japan had not yet paid attention to this, so the development of the industry was quite smooth. However, this smooth development trend soon began to suffer setbacks, for two reasons: one was the irrational domestic tariff system, and the other was that neighboring Japan rose up to imitate and compete. A brief description is given below for the reference of the Chinese people.

According to my country's tariff system at that time, all domestic products purchased and used by Chinese merchants, in addition to paying the regular tax at the place of purchase and loading, must also pay the arrival tax (that is, the tax levied at the place of arrival); when foreign merchants purchased, they only need to pay one tax, which can be directly transported abroad. This is the result of unequal treaty restrictions. At that time, Japan, due to its relatively developed scientific knowledge, already knew that all kinds of oil cakes (mainly cottonseed cakes) were good products for fertilizing fields, and purchased a lot from China every year; later, in view of the fact that oil cakes are the remnants after extracting vegetable oil seeds, their selling price often includes the double tax paid by Chinese merchants on pamphlets, which is not as good as transporting oil seeds out of the country to make oil and cakes themselves, paying a single tax is more advantageous. Therefore, it began to operate new-style oil extraction within the country. Since the 20th year of Guangxu, Japan's cottonseed oil extraction plants have been established one after another, and the threat to the local national oil extraction industry has become increasingly serious, leading to closures and reorganizations. This is not only because Japan can make its own cottonseed oil and cottonseed cake, but also because my country's cottonseed raw materials are purchased in large quantities, resulting in insufficient raw materials for domestic factories. This kind of past historical record should be paid attention to by all those who are concerned about the history of the development of national industry. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, the oil extraction industry has developed, but its momentum is very slow. After the fall of the Northeast, my country's oil extraction industry was even more severely hit. The Northeast is a concentrated production area of soybeans, and the oil extraction industry in Dalian and Shenyang is far superior to that in Shanghai, but now they are no longer ours! Recently, Japan has strengthened its control over Manchurian agricultural products, and at the same time concluded a German-German trade agreement to exchange a large number of soybeans from the Northeast for German ordnance, making our local area even more lacking in these agricultural products. For example, the recent decision of the local tofu industry to raise prices is one of its reflections. Therefore, it is natural that the oil extraction industry in Shanghai (mainly referring to the extraction of soybean oil) will suffer a huge impact, and this is also the way we should plan to prevent it. (To be continued)

Local Organizations of this City Yesterday Gave a Farewell Party to the World Games Delegation; Director Pan, Yang Xiaotian, and Others Gave Speeches; Delegation to Depart Tomorrow Afternoon by Ship 153

The delegation representing our country at the World Games is scheduled to depart tomorrow afternoon on the Italian ship Conte Verde. Various circles in this city held a farewell reception at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA yesterday at 4 p.m. Mayor Wu, represented by Director Pan Gongzhan, and others gave speeches. Details are recorded as follows:

Participating Representatives: Mayor Wu (represented by Director Pan), Chu Minyi, Li Dachao of the Municipal Government, Tong Xingbai of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Yang Xiaotian of the Garrison Headquarters, Jiang Bai of the Education Bureau, Director Cai of the Public Security Bureau, Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Council, Song Huanzhang of the China Insurance Company, as well as representatives from the Social Bureau, Municipal Agricultural Association, China Cultural Construction Association, Municipal Sports Association, Municipal Stadium, major Physical Education Associations, Vocational Education Society, YMCA, Jingwu Association, National Arts Hall, Central Research Institute, Local Association, Aviation Association, Diligent Sports Monthly Magazine, Eurasia Aviation Corporation, representatives of over two hundred people from the Two-Roads Bureau, Lingnan University, Jiaotong University, Great China University, Sino-French Institute of Technology, East Asia University, Liangjiang, Commercial Press, Zhongxi Pharmacy, Tianchu MSG Factory, Zhenjiang Fellow Villagers Association, and other groups, including Yu Zhenhui, Zhou Bangjun, Wu Yun Chu, Ma Chonggan, Zhou Hanmei, Wu Zijing, He De Kui, and representatives of various newspapers and organizations.

Chairman's Speech: Chairman Yang Xiaotian said in his speech, roughly: "You are honored to represent China at the World Games. I am making a small contribution to express my warm send-off. China's technological backwardness in participating in the World Games is undeniable. Therefore, in addition to technical competition, our goal is to pay attention to other people's techniques for observation and learning. At the same time, we should pay special attention to two points in terms of spirit: one is the cultivation of personal character and the maintenance of order in life; the other is the observance of the spirit of unity and public discipline. These two points are the central principles of participating in sports. If we can do this, we will make progress technically. I wish you all to bring back the trophy of victory from the World Games, and I hope to bring the great spirit and culture of the Chinese nation to people all over the world."

Speeches from Various Circles: Tong Xingbai of the Municipal Party Headquarters said in his speech: "Our participation in the World Games should be based on the principle of neither arrogance nor inferiority, to visit the international stage, learn from others' strengths, make up for our shortcomings, and promote our strengths to contribute to the world. We must use facts to show others and improve the country's status. And I hope everyone will pay attention to things other than sports at all times, and carefully note the construction of his spirit as a lesson for the revival of China." Song Huanzhang of China Insurance Company said, "I hope that we will not be proud of our victory, and strive for excellence; if we fail, we do not need to regret, and continue to work hard." He De Kui of the Public Works Bureau said, "In addition to physical health, we should pay attention to mental health, mutual assistance and cooperation, and add glory to the country."

Mayor's Speech: Mayor Wu, represented by Director Pan, said in his speech: "Our country's participation in the World Games does not necessarily mean complete victory, nor can we be discouraged because we may not get a victory. The victory of sports lies entirely in the efforts of ordinary days. This time, we will contribute our ability on the one hand and visit the strengths of others on the other. Of course, it is not a luxury to have to win. Our group can show the spirit of a great country to Germany and the countries we pass through, and it is a great success. Because foreign countries do not understand China, if we show ourselves everywhere as a modern national, we can improve China's international status. This kind of harvest is more valuable than getting a trophy. Therefore, the only hope is that everyone will take care of the national character of the whole country, so that China can improve its international status, and a grand welcome to you all when we return."

Representative's Reply: Finally, Shen Siliang, on behalf of the delegation, replied: "We are very grateful to all circles for the grand farewell today. This trip abroad is a great responsibility. I believe everyone can do their best, and every move will show the good phenomena of the Chinese nation, so as not to disappoint everyone's expectations. China has only paid attention to sports in the past 20 years. I remember that at the World Games eight years ago, our country had no athletes to participate, only one representative. At the World Games four years ago, only one athlete participated. This time, there are more than 70 athletes participating, more than 40 members of the visiting group, and more than 10 staff members, for a total of more than 100 people. The number has increased from one person to more than one hundred in four years, which cannot be said to be progress. This time, the government subsidizes 170,000 yuan, and donations from various parties amount to 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. The cost of going abroad is nearly 250,000 yuan, which is far less than other countries, but I believe that everyone will be able to show some achievements when they go abroad to comfort the people of the country."

Sailing Tomorrow Afternoon: The delegation has decided to sail on the Italian ship Conte Verde at 12:00 noon tomorrow (June 16) at the North Station of the China Merchants Bureau. At that time, representatives from all walks of life will go to the port to say goodbye at 10:00 a.m. The Garrison Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau will send bands to play music, and the Aviation Association will send a plane to see them off to Wusongkou.

World Games, Britain Also Requests to Host the Next Games; Motivation Comes from the Banking Sector 159

Havas Agency, London, 23rd - Regarding the location of the 12th Olympic Games in 1940, Britain, Japan, and Finland are now competing. Henry Hunt, Secretary of the British Olympic Association, recently issued a statement on this matter in a private capacity, saying that when the 10th Olympic Games were held in Los Angeles, USA in 1932, most countries advocated that the 1940 Games should be held in Europe again, and the 13th Games in 1944 could be held in other continents. Therefore, when the International Olympic Committee meets to discuss this issue, most countries will naturally oppose Japan and choose one of Britain and Finland to host the 1940 Olympic Games.

Havas Agency, London, 23rd - Regarding the location of the 12th Olympic Games, that is, the next Olympic Games, Japan and Italy have successively requested to hold the Games in their countries, and Finland then followed suit. It is now learned that Britain also intends to make the same request. Although Britain's move may attract the attention of small countries in the European continent, most members of the Olympic Committee may not vote in favor when it is submitted for a vote in the future. The 1908 Olympic Games were originally planned to be held in Rome, but due to Italy's lack of preparation, it was temporarily changed to be held in Britain. At that time, most countries, such as Japan and Finland, had not yet officially participated. It has been 28 years since 1908. If Britain asks to host the next Games at this time, there is nothing wrong with it. However, the winter competition program is inconvenient to be held in Britain, which is a pity for most people. The country may propose to hold the winter competition program in Switzerland, and hold other programs in the country. According to those who are familiar with the details, the proposal for Britain to request to hold the next Games in the country does not originate from the sports world, but is initiated by the banking sector. They expect that the gathering of spectators will triple the British business. Witnessing the grand occasion of the 25th anniversary of the accession of the late King George V last year, they are encouraging the government and are not worried about not having anything to say. However, the major newspapers in the capital are not paying much attention to it.

Education News

Chinese-English Junior High School History and Geography Textbooks, Two Kinds of Bonuses are Set at 6,000 Yuan Each; Deadline for Submissions is the End of This Year 164

The Management Board of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund is soliciting junior high school history and geography textbooks. To encourage compilation, two kinds of bonuses are set up. One is for junior high school history textbooks, with a bonus of 6,000 yuan. The other is for junior high school geography textbooks, also with a bonus of 6,000 yuan. The compilation of these two textbooks must be in accordance with the middle school curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education in November 1922. Manuscripts should be sealed and sent to the association's office (78 Shanxi Road, Nanjing) before December 20, 1936. Manuscripts should include a detailed table of contents, and the font is not limited, but it must be clearly written. If the manuscript is introduced by a group, the group should provide a separate certificate. For the sake of prudence, the Association decided to hire experts to form a review committee to be responsible for the review. The selected manuscripts will still be sent to the Ministry of Education for approval. The results will be announced and announced on March 1, 1937. Unselected manuscripts will be returned.

The meeting was chaired by Tong Xingmen and recorded by Fan Kanru. Many important matters were resolved, such as the production of teaching materials, the formulation of work outlines and detailed rules, the specification of clothing styles and camp flags and badges for boys and girls, and the establishment of opening procedures and order, etc., until the bell rang eight times before the meeting adjourned.

Former Labor University Shanghai Alumni Association Established 172

The former National Labor University was ordered to close by the Executive Yuan in July 1932, and four years have passed since. The alumni are scattered in various provinces and cities, serving social institutions and earning a good reputation. There are over one hundred alumni in Shanghai alone. In order to connect and strengthen their friendships and further their studies, representatives were appointed to prepare for the organization of the Labor University Shanghai Alumni Association. The inaugural meeting was held yesterday at the Pan Family Garden in Jiangwan. In addition to passing the charter, Tang Ying, Sun Letao, Wang Yingming, Li Chongpu, Wang Rulin, Ding Jingxin, Wu Jindi, Sun Kexing, and Zhu Fan were elected as directors.

Therefore, merchants who had previously advanced the goods are now tightening their sales. Yesterday, market prices were rising sharply. The quoted price for Gaozhuang Xinning supplement goods was 25 yuan, unified hand goods were 24 yuan, Gao Chen goods were 34 yuan, ordinary goods were 32 yuan, Yantai Dabeibei medulla ossea was 52 yuan, medium pieces were 50 yuan, and Jiangbei medulla ossea was 45 yuan. Market conditions are very firm.

(Jellyfish) New goods will have to wait until next month to be available on the market. The inventory of old goods is already thin, and selling prices are rising. Currently, the original price of Yangshan goods is 11 yuan, and after processing, it is 11 yuan and 3 jiao. Goods from Sijiao and Huanglong, etc., can be reduced by 5 jiao. In the future, we will see how the new goods from various mountains are produced, and then divide the market's prosperity or decline.

(Squid) New hot-water goods have not yet arrived. Due to the occasional procurement by merchants from Sichuan, Hankou, Shantou, and Guangdong, the old goods in stock have turned upward. Yesterday, the brokerage house opened prices: Jinshan bucket squid, 62 pieces, price 77 yuan; Xiangguan Qiushui squid, market disc selling 85 or 86 yuan. If the new goods are late, there is still a trend of continued increase.

Sugar Market: Sharp Decline in Transactions for Guangdong Sugar Standards 192

Anhai Brown Sugar Continues to Remain Closed

Yesterday, the currency market trend remained flat and soft, and transactions were few. The association marked the price of No. 24 coarse granulated white spot goods at 22 yuan and 1 jiao, transshipped goods at 6 yuan and 8 jiao, and the quoted prices for Dongchi white, as well as this factory's cotton white, Zhenji, Zhenyu, Dahua, and Jinxin, were as before. Transactions were sparse. The brokerage market only opened for 160 bags of Mianchi sugar from the Chaozhou merchant group, with the higher grade at 12 yuan and 5 jiao and a half, and the lower grade at 12 yuan and 2 jiao to 1 jiao. Anhai red is slightly tighter near the market. Since the brokerage side was unwilling to compromise, and the merchant side was unwilling to add more, a stalemate formed, and no transaction was made.

The joint-stock company reached the second tender exchange period this week, with a total quota of 8,342 bags of Guangdong coarse white, etc. However, as a result of low merchant appetite, only 400 bags were traded. 310 bags of Shunde factory Five Rams coarse white were sold at 21 yuan and 5 jiao, 10 bags of Dongguan factory were also sold at 21 yuan and 5 jiao, 20 bags of sandy white in the city were sold at 19 yuan and 3 jiao, 50 bags of No. 2 cotton white were sold at 20 yuan and 6 jiao, and another 10 bags of No. 4 were sold at 20 yuan and 4 jiao. The original price of Quxi coarse white was not traded.

Popular Lectures

Wang Sun Jia's Mother 193

— Zheng Kan Ci

—"If a child understands self-reliance, the state of Qi will not perish!"—

In the dim twilight, an old woman with completely white hair, leaning on a cane, stood falteringly at the entrance of an alley. She had been standing there for a long time, her legs aching. When she first came out, the people on the street wore worried expressions, milling about in groups, leading their children and carrying their women, heading northeast (from Ju to Jimo). She had originally wanted to ask if some kind of emergency had occurred, but thinking of a lone city surrounded by enemies, she figured that emergencies were to be expected and didn't ask. Her only hope now was that her son would return soon, so the two of them could be together, putting her mind at ease whether they lived or died. The noisy street prevented her from thinking calmly. She aimlessly looked at this group, then at that group, but no deep impression was made. A streak of beautiful evening sun flashed over the wall, and the scene before her immediately became blurred. At the same time, the number of people on the street dwindled, and the loneliness of dusk made her reflect on everything in the past. She sighed softly, "Alas! If Jia'er's (referring to the old woman's son, Wang Sun Jia) father were still alive, the state of Qi would not be in such a state."

She suddenly remembered something that had happened thirty-one years ago (the first year of King Nan of Zhou – 314 BC) – the day the Qi army broke through the state of Yan, and news of the victory arrived. The Qi court and the general public celebrated as if they were going mad. Some idle politicians and short-sighted military men said, "We in Qi are lucky. If we get Yan, we might be able to replace the Zhou dynasty! We are acting on behalf of the people to punish evildoers and practice the way of the king!" At that time, Wang Sun Jia's father was a minister under King Xuan of Qi. Although he, like other ministers, went to court to offer congratulations, he felt a sense of unease, because he did not agree with Qi's opportunistic and exploitative way of being king. He wanted to say something fair on behalf of the people of Yan, but everyone was so intoxicated with joy that no one would listen to him. He could only stand in the court assembly as if in a daze, pursing his lips without saying a word.

At that time, Mencius happened to be a guest minister in Qi. King Yi of Qi respected him very much and sent Jia's father to invite him to court to discuss the major plan for dealing with the state of Yan. Jia's father was rushed and unable to say much, but on the way, he could only say to Mencius, "Master, please say something fair!" Mencius did not understand his feelings and thought he was just being polite, so he pretended not to hear and didn't even look at him. Because the state of Qi had been prosperous for a long time, it was accustomed to swallowing the weak and bullying the small, creating a deceptive philosophy of the strong: clearly practicing the way of the hegemon, but claiming to be practicing the way of the king; clearly invading others, but claiming to be saving them. Mencius thought that Jia's father's talk of fairness was nothing more than empty rhetoric, so he ignored him.

When Mencius arrived at the court, King Qi rose to greet him and asked him happily, "We have already defeated the state of Yan and corrected that Yan Kuai who brought disaster to the country and harmed the people. Now, some people advise me not to take Yan, while others advise me to take it. I think that attacking a state of ten thousand chariots with a state of ten thousand chariots, and conquering it in fifty days, could not have been achieved by human power alone. I am afraid it is the will of Heaven. Not taking it will surely incur the wrath of Heaven, but what should I do if I take it?" Mencius thought to himself, "Good method! The king is again using the will of Heaven to cover up his tyranny!" He did not want to interrupt King Qi directly, so he answered very tactfully, "If the people of Yan are happy to have you take it, then take it. In ancient times, there was a King Wu who did the same. If the people of Yan are not happy to have you take it, please do not take it. In ancient times, there was a King Wen who did the same." King Xuan of Qi said, "I cannot concern myself with whether the people are happy or not. I only fear that the various states will not allow me to swallow a large country alone and will unite to save Yan." Mencius said, " 'A thousand people pointing fingers, even without illness, one will die.' How much more so with the tens of millions of people of Yan? How can you not care about them? At the same time, it is possible that the various states will form an alliance to plot against Qi. The states were originally afraid of Qi's strength, and now that Qi has doubled in size, it is like a tiger with wings. Each state is in danger, so how can they not unite to attack Qi? If Qi wants to avoid disaster, it must abandon Yan. Please consider this carefully, my King!" After Mencius finished speaking, he bowed and left.

Jia's father believed that everything Mencius said was perfectly reasonable and conveyed it to his wife, Lady Jia, at home, adding some of his own thoughts: "Both Qi and Yan were established very early, and they have been able to exist until today, so of course they have their reasons for existing. How can we be blind to the overall situation, be greedy for merit and profit, and make enemies of the people of Yan? Although they are temporarily subdued by us, they will one day rise up in resistance. When that time comes, Qi will be in trouble! The state of Qin originally had the ambition to annex all under Heaven, and the state of Chu's ambitions are not small either. Han, Zhao, and Wei often base their diplomacy on that of Qin and Chu, so they are rarely reliable. Once the Yan disaster breaks out, Qi will be isolated and may even perish!" Jia's father couldn't help but shed tears.

His wife quickly comforted him, "Sir, the state of Qi will certainly not perish. Please don't be sad!" Jia's father asked, "How do you know?" His wife said, "There is no disaster in the world that cannot be prevented. The most fearful thing is not seeing it beforehand, or seeing it too late, when there is no time to prevent it. You have already seen the root of Qi's disaster. As long as we take preventive measures early, what is there to fear?" Jia's father said, "I know that, but one person's strength is limited. If everyone doesn't cooperate with you, you can't do anything. We are doing something that is opportunistic and exploitative, so everyone is extremely happy. No one will want to hear you say such killjoy things." His wife said, "There's no need to worry about that. No matter what great thing you do, it usually starts with one or two people initiating it, striving and struggling, and gradually attracting attention, gaining support, and creating a new atmosphere that can help this thing succeed. Why don't you become such a pioneer who transforms the atmosphere and awakens the people to save the country?"

Jia's father kept his wife's words in his heart and worked to save Qi with unwavering determination. He also tried to persuade King Xuan of Qi to rein in his ambition to invade and burn others, but unfortunately, King Xuan did not listen, and instead scolded Jia's father, "Mencius is a foreigner, so I don't blame him for not thinking of Qi. You are a person of Qi, yet you say such cold things, you deserve to die!" The king then distanced himself from Jia's father and implemented the annexation of the state of Yan. Unexpectedly, the people of Yan refused to submit and rose up in resistance, driving the Qi army out of their territory. From then on, Yan hated Qi to the bone and plotted to attack Linzi (the capital of Qi) to avenge their humiliation. King Xuan of Qi saw that Jia's father had foresight and gradually came to trust him.

Jia's father paid close attention to the defense against Yan. He often said to King Xuan of Qi, "The King of Yan has the ambition of Goujian to avenge Wu. On the surface, he is still on good terms with us, but in his heart, he is difficult to fathom. We must be on guard. I hope that Your Majesty will repair our internal affairs, strengthen our border defenses, and treat our neighboring countries generously so that Yan has no opportunity to exploit. Only then can Qi avoid disaster. Qi is surrounded by crises today, and it is not a time for us to rest easy. I urge Your Majesty to intensify our preparations!" King Xuan indeed listened to Jia's father and worked hard to improve governance.

On the other side, the King of Yan (Kuai's son, King Zhao) was indeed like King Goujian of Yue, enduring hardship and biding his time. He wore tattered clothes, ate coarse food, and saved money to support orphans and widows, cultivate young people, and work hard to rebuild the broken state of Yan. Then, he humbled himself, offered generous gifts, and recruited talented people, seeking ways to take revenge. At that time, there was a wise man in Yan named Guo Wei. The King of Yan went to his home to ask for advice, saying, "Qi took advantage of the internal strife in our country and took the opportunity to attack and break through Yan. Not a single person in Yan does not consider this a disgrace and hate Qi to the core. I know that Yan is small and lacks strength, making it difficult to take revenge on Qi. I wish to work together with wise men to govern the country and wash away the shame of our former kings. I don't know how to avenge the state's enmity. Please, sir, instruct me!"

Guo Wei saw that the King of Yan had respectfully come to him for advice, so he frankly told him, "The most important thing is to obtain talented people. The one who associates with an emperor is his teacher; the one who associates with a king is his friend; the one who associates with a hegemon is his minister; the one who associates with the ruler of a fallen kingdom is his servant. If you break down your prejudices, treat people with humility, and receive instruction from the north, then someone a hundred times better than yourself will come; if you walk before others and rest after others, first asking for instruction and then remaining silent, then someone ten times better than yourself will come; if others walk before you and you follow behind, then someone equal to yourself will come; if you lean on your armrest, lean on your cane, don't even look at people, and arbitrarily order people around, then only servants will be willing to come; if you lose your temper and beat and scold people, then only slaves will be willing to come!—This is the method of attracting scholars in ancient times. If the King can truly widely select the wise men in the country and hold audiences with their followers, and the world hears that the King holds audiences with wise ministers, then many wise men will surely flock to Yan." King Zhao said, "Who should I hold audiences with?" Guo Wei said, "I have heard that in ancient times, there was a ruler who offered a thousand pieces of gold to find a thousand-mile horse, but he could not find one for three years. His eunuch said to him, 'Please send your servant out to find one!' The ruler then sent him out. This eunuch spent three months and indeed found a thousand-mile horse. But unfortunately, this horse had already died, so he spent five hundred pieces of gold to buy the horse's bones and report back. When the ruler saw this, he was very angry and said, 'I want a living horse, why spend five hundred pieces of gold to buy a dead horse?' The eunuch replied, 'You are willing to spend five hundred pieces of gold to buy a dead horse, how much more so for a living horse? All those who sell good horses will surely say that the King is able to buy horses and will send good horses to you.' Sure enough, before a year had passed, people were sending three thousand-mile horses to sell. If the King truly wants to attract scholars, please start with Wei. Even though Wei is unworthy, the King still treats him with respect, how much more so someone wiser than Wei? When the wise men of the world see that the King respects scholars in this way, they will surely come from a thousand miles away."

King Zhao listened to Guo Wei's words and built a palace for Guo Wei to live in, treating him with the respect due to a teacher. When the scholars of the world heard that King Zhao respected wise men, they all competed to come to Yan! Yue Yi came from the state of Wei, Zou Yan came from the state of Qi, Ju Xin came from the state of Zhao... King Zhao used their policies and spent twenty-eight years governing the state of Yan well. Then, he appointed Yue Yi as the supreme general and conspired with Qin, Chu, Han, Zhao, and Wei to attack Qi in place of them. The Qi army was defeated, and King Min of Qi fled to the city of Ju. The Yan army chased after them, breaking into Linzi, looting the treasures of Qi, and burning the rich mansions and ancestral temples of Qi. Of the seventy or so cities of Qi, only Ju and Jimo were not captured by the Yan army.

At that time, Jia's father had already been dead for more than ten years, and his son, Wang Sun Jia, was only fifteen years old. After Jia's father died, King Min of Qi had no one to warn him, and he gradually became dissolute and neglected to prepare for Yan, so he suffered a complete defeat. Jia's mother still hoped that he could recall Jia's father's policies, regain his spirit, and recover the lost territory. Therefore, she wanted to send her underage son to serve the troubled and powerless king.

She only had one son, Wang Sun Jia, whom she had given birth to when she was over forty years old, so she would naturally cherish him more than other mothers. If she did not love her country, how could she bear to send such a young son to take on such a dangerous and important task? She decided to send her son to take up the post that day, but her son did not yet know. He got up in the morning, still wearing his short hair, dressed in children's clothes with narrow sleeves and short legs. After greeting his mother good morning, he returned to his study to read. Jia's mother saw her son's thin back and couldn't help but shed tears like rain, silently thinking: "Useful people (referring to Jia's father) always die young, leaving behind such a small chicken that is not worth much, what can he do! He is also especially thinner and smaller than others. Relatives all say that I pressure him too much with his studies, ruining my son. If they knew that today I would have him put down his books and, in a lone city surrounded by enemies, risk his life to defend the country, I don't know what they would say about me. Alas! I can't worry about so much, surely I love my son just as much as anyone else? But none of them think as thoroughly as I do for him. Anyone with any spirit would rather die than be a slave to a fallen nation, much less my son? He is a tiger cub, he is a lion cub, he wants to leap out and devour his enemies. He can't be like a pig, huddled in a pen, allowing himself to be slaughtered..." Thinking of this, her courage was a hundred times greater, and she herself seemed to become young and strong again. She didn't even need her cane and walked briskly into the clothing room, took out Jia's father's court clothes, shortened them by a few inches, and barely managed to fit them on her son.

While Jia's mother was tying up her son's hair, she instructed him, "Son, the country has been bullied by the state of Yan to the point of being unrecognizable. Our land has almost been completely seized, and who knows how many people have been killed. If we don't unite and resist and recover our lost territory, we will become slaves to a fallen nation." Wang Sun Jia quickly said, "Mom, I can't be a slave to a fallen nation!" Jia's mother said, "Yes! You can't be a slave to a fallen nation, I can't be a slave to a fallen nation, and all the people of Qi can't be slaves to a fallen nation. That's why I want you to go out and save the country. The country is in urgent need of you and doesn't have time to wait for you to grow up." Wang Sun Jia said, "Mom, I've already grown up. Please don't always treat me like a child. Actually, what is the difference between adult and child? The one who can accomplish great things is an adult, otherwise, even if he is a hundred years old, I would say he is a child.—Mom, haven't you seen wolves and sheep? Wolves are smaller than sheep, but when sheep hear the sound of a wolf, they are so frightened that they can't move and allow themselves to be devoured by the wolf. How can we be arrogant because of our size and give up on ourselves because of our smallness?" When Jia's mother heard her son's words, she said happily, "If a child understands self-reliance, the state of Qi will not perish! The state of Qi will not perish!"

Wang Sun Jia went out to work, leaving early in the morning and returning late at night. Jia's mother, because she loved her son so much, would go out to the entrance of the alley to wait for her son as soon as she finished lunch. She would always stand for several hours every day before she saw her son return. Sometimes the news was bad, and she was worried about her son and couldn't put her mind at ease. Often, she would send her son out in the morning and, if he didn't come back, she would stand and wait all day. People nearby were used to it, and when they saw her silhouette in the distance, they knew it was her. One day, an old man named Wang, who was well-informed, saw that it was getting dark and Jia's mother was still standing at the entrance of the alley. He knew that her son had not yet returned and was very worried about her.

It turned out that a few days earlier, the state of Chu, resentful that the state of Yan had not divided the spoils fairly, had specially sent Nuo Chi to supervise a large army to Ju, ostensibly to save Qi, but in reality, to use force to force the state of Yan to divide the land and looted treasures of Qi equally with the state of Chu. King Min of Qi did not know of Nuo Chi's treacherous plot and opened the gates to let him into the city of Ju. In the first few days, he pretended to discuss plans for attack and defense with the King of Qi, but later he impolitely killed the King of Qi. When this news spread, some timid people of Qi, fearing that they could not stand their ground in Ju, fled to Jimo one after another. Wang Sun Jia, because he was unaware of the situation, still went to court on the day the King of Qi was killed. Old Man Wang, fearing that Jia's mother would worry, dared not tell her the truth, but only asked, "Old Madam, has Jia-ge'er not returned yet?"

"Old Man Wang, I don't know why Jia'er hasn't returned so late.—Is there any bad news?" Jia's mother asked.

Old Man Wang couldn't help but reveal a little news, saying, "I heard that Nuo Chi, sent by the state of Chu, is making things difficult for (he dared not say "killed") our king. Maybe there's something going on in the court, and Ge'er can't come back tonight. Old Madam, you should go home and rest."

Jia's mother thought that Old Man Wang's words made sense, thanked him, and slowly walked back. She had just arrived home when Wang Sun Jia also staggered back. Jia's mother quickly asked, "Where is the King of Qi?" Wang Sun Jia, fearing that his mother would be upset, dared not tell the truth, but stammered, "Um, you're asking about the King? Um—I don't know where the King went. I looked for him all day but couldn't find him, so I came back to see if you were worried." Jia's mother said angrily, "You useless child, what did you come back for?" She was so angry that she couldn't speak. After a while, she continued, "You serve the King, and the King has fled, but you don't know where the King is. How could you come back! I used to think you were a good child, knowing how to be loyal and righteous, so I especially loved you. You leave early in the morning and return late at night, and I would always go to the front door to wait for you. If you went out at night and didn't return, I would always go to the entrance of the alley to wait for you. Recently, because the country is in an emergency, I have been even more worried about you. No matter whether you left early or late, I would always stand at the entrance of the alley early to wait for you. If I had known you were so useless, why would I have put so much effort into you?"

When Wang Sun Jia heard his mother's words of blame, he quickly knelt down to explain, "How could I be so unfaithful and unrighteous? But the courtiers have all been bribed by Nuo Chi, and there is no one to discuss anything with..." Jia's mother interrupted her son before he could finish speaking and retorted, "You really don't understand! You still want to discuss saving the King and saving the country with the courtiers? If they were good people, the country wouldn't be in such a mess. I dare say that most of those in high positions today are like spies. There are very few reliable people. Why don't you go to the people to find truly patriotic and righteous people? The people of Qi are an excellent race, and there must be many people with spirit. If you can gather them, it won't be difficult to restore the state of Qi."

Wang Sun Jia bade farewell to his mother and immediately went into the city again. When he reached the city wall, the soldiers guarding the city refused to open the gate because it was dark. Fearing that he would anger his mother again, he dared not go home and stood under the city wall overnight. When the city gate opened at dawn, he ran to the market to call on the masses. He obtained permission from a butcher who slaughtered cattle to stand high on the meat stand and give a speech. He said loudly, "Everyone, uncles, aunts, brothers, and sisters, we people of Qi have been bullied by foreigners to the point where we can't bear it any longer..." When the crowd saw Wang Sun Jia, a small person wearing adult clothes, with a gauze hat covering his eyebrows, the collar touching the brim of his hat, revealing half of his small white face, just like dressing up a monkey, they couldn't help but laugh. But when they heard him talk about the country being humiliated, everyone became serious, stopped all buying and selling, and gathered around, listening attentively. Wang Sun Jia continued, "The country has more than seventy cities, all of which have been seized by the state of Yan, leaving only Ju and Jimo. We must rely on these two cities as a base to recover our lost territory. But now we are being controlled by Chu. Ever since Nuo Chi entered the city of Ju, Ju has not been part of Qi. Today, Nuo Chi killed our king. If we don't kill Nuo Chi, there is no hope for the restoration of Qi!" The crowd, holding back their tears, jumped up and said, "Kill Nuo Chi! Kill Nuo Chi!" Wang Sun Jia said, "Yes, I plan to go kill Nuo Chi. If any of you are willing to go with me, please take off your clothes and expose your right arm!"

So, more than four hundred people in the entire city, including Wang Sun Jia, exposed their right arms. Those with knives took knives, those with sticks took sticks, and they all went to Nuo Chi's camp to behead him and display his head to the public. The Chu soldiers were either killed, fled, or surrendered, and the city of Ju was restored in an instant. When the people of Qi near and far heard this news of victory, they all rubbed their fists and sharpened their palms, eager to try. Soon after, Tian Dan launched an uprising in Jimo in response, and quickly restored the entire state of Qi. This was all thanks to the ethnic revolution in the city of Ju, which inspired morale.

On the day of the successful revolution, after the great events were completed, the masses surrounded Wang Sun Jia and took him home to pay respects to his mother. Jia's mother stood at the entrance of the alley to welcome them. The crowd cheered thunderously, making Jia's mother so happy that she shed tears.
