Biographies of Exemplary Women: Wang Sun Jia's Mother

The Publishing World

Early Human Society 194

— Shimizu

Translated by Lü Shuxiang, Price: $1.50

Standard Book of the Week, Published by Commercial Press

Robert Heinrich Lowie (1883—?) is a moderate scholar in contemporary "anthropology." Although his research area is limited to the Americas, he has collected a vast amount of materials and published numerous works. He analyzes things with a calm mind and a scientific perspective, not bound by past theories, and has made contributions and inventions. He does not regard civilized tribes as the chosen ones, thus looking down upon tribes with backward cultures in the same era. As a result, he published "Primitive Society" (1920) and "Are We Civilized?" (Ae We Civilizen, 1929). "Are We Civilized?" can help us understand that many of our current daily lives and customs come from primitive people, so we no longer dare to despise the culturally backward peoples of our time. Mr. Zhou Zuoren, a famous Chinese scholar, once said that this book is self-explanatory. What about "Primitive Society"? It is simply an excellent book, although it was published sixteen years ago, its value is still high. Especially for those engaged in "ethnology" and "anthropology," this book, which describes the truth and reality of early human society with a calm mind and fair perspective, enumerates the factors of the cultural history of early human society, and criticizes the inadequacy of the "evolutionary school" of thought, is a concise and lucid good book, and it is necessary to read it carefully.

Everyone knows the influence of the evolutionary school of thought in China in the past, and everyone knows the influence of L.H. Morgan's masterpiece "Ancient Society" in China, which was regarded as the ultimate truth. In fact, this is far from the truth. Morgan's book was published in 1877, when the study of "anthropology" and "ethnology" was not yet very enlightened. He took the evolutionary viewpoint as the premise, included all the complex situations of primitive society, regardless of black and white, and summarized them in a simple way, and then used this to discuss all early human cultures, seeking their slightest similarities, discarding most of the differences, fragmenting cultures, disregarding the whole picture, and forcibly mixing many early human cultures with different cultural histories and factors into one pile, and including them in the same type. How can this be considered appropriate?

We should know that "hypothesis" is not impossible, but all kinds of conditions must be met. "Arrangement" is also possible, but it cannot be based on accidental phenomena. "Culture" has a certain order and level in the excavated strata, which can be used to discover the construction process of early human culture. "Culture" is an organism, with many superficially similar phenomena, but they are not created by the same cause. Conversely, fixed cultural factors can produce one or more different phenomena. How can we insist on one and use it to exemplify the rest? Also, some cultures are accidentally the same, based on the similarity of primitive psychology; or only a small point of similarity. If we are unwilling to find its source calmly and rationally, regardless of its geographical environment, time, and space, and insist that it is completely the same because of a small point of similarity, and then think that it is the same type and discuss it, this is really arbitrary. Moreover, the different cultural processes are different due to their cultural backgrounds, and it is not necessarily the case that every century progresses to the same field; and it is not necessarily the case that they all follow the same path. It is impossible to assert that "matriarchal society" must precede "patriarchal society" based on accidental discoveries. Most things in the world are unpredictable, and it is a joke to unify the extremely complex early human society and early human culture with a simple model. The process of cultural development cannot be separated from the geographical environment. Because of this, its progress is slow or fast, and there are examples of squeezing without advancing or retreating. The different paths are not entirely due to one path, and there is no need to elaborate on them. How can one obtain great inventions that are in line with the actual situation by using the "evolutionary" perspective and methods?

Lowie carefully lists various systems, customs, and beliefs of early human society, extensively quoting and using lucid language to expose the shortcomings of Morgan's theory, which is convincing. He chapter by chapter examines Morgan's errors, based on facts, to restore them to their original appearance, without bias or arbitrariness, so that readers are stunned, not only feeling his vast knowledge, but also feeling his insightful views. He said: "Contemporary anthropologists have discovered many new knowledge and new methods, and Morgan's great work has become 'old fashioned'." After reading "Primitive Society" carefully, Lowie's words are indeed the truth, not boasting, nor a slander of the predecessors with deep self-expectation!

In this book, each chapter has countless examples, clearly and lucidly described, to prove the inadequacy of the "evolutionary school," to establish his own claim of explaining "culture" with "culture," and explaining the past cultural history and current cultural status with "cultural history" and "cultural environment," comprehensively and cautiously, with thoroughness and expertise, it can be said to be a book worth recommending.

Naturally, the first and last two chapters of this book are about "ethnology" and "anthropology" in general, but the discussions in these chapters are enough to show the author's claims, to refute the shortcomings of the "evolutionary theory" and "diffusion theory" of the "evolutionary school," for those who are new to this field, these two chapters are very important texts, and it is best to read them slowly and carefully. The chapters in the second half on social organization are detailed and meticulous, with rich materials and clear descriptions, which can be considered the most brilliant part of the book, and the author sincerely introduces it to all readers.

Introducing a Book on Chinese Rhetoric 195

— Zhong Yi

When it comes to Chinese literary critics, it seems that besides a few famous names such as Liu Xie and Zhong Rong, there are hardly any others, but this is because we have not studied carefully. In the wilderness, among the abandoned group, there are many great critics! What I want to introduce now is one of them.

First, let us know his background.

Chen Kui, a native of Linhai in the Southern Song Dynasty, styled Shujin, was the first in the imperial examination in Shaoxing. During the reign of Emperor Guangzong, he served as the Vice Minister of the Ministry of Personnel. During the reign of Emperor Ningzong, he served as the Assistant Administrator of the Privy Council concurrently. He served in high positions, but was later dismissed from office for offending Han Tuozhou. He wrote two books, "Southern Song Dynasty Court Records" and "Wen Ze," and "Wen Ze" is his major work on essays.

"Wen Ze" is a book that does not have a separate edition now, and is included in the Taizhou Series. The content of this book is mostly about the rhetoric of essays, and it is described in the most detail and completeness in chapters C and D.

Regarding rhetoric from the West, there is the so-called "metaphor." Chen Kui, in chapter C of this book, said that there are ten kinds of metaphors. I will now re-introduce a little.

First, is direct metaphor. He said: "First is direct metaphor, saying 'like', 'as if', 'as', or 'similar', which is clearly visible." And he gave examples of "climbing trees to catch fish," "rotten wood driving six horses," and "like the North Star, with all the stars revolving around it."

Second, is hidden metaphor. He said: "Second is hidden metaphor, although the text is hidden, the meaning can be found." And he gave examples of "Where can he flee to avoid it?" and "Is that Wu?" (Zuo Zhuan).

Third, is analogy. He said: "Third is analogy, taking one category to metaphorize it in order." And he gave the example of "The emperor is like a hall, the ministers are like steps, and the common people are like the ground" (Jia Yi's New Book).

Fourth, is rhetorical metaphor. He said: "Fourth is rhetorical metaphor, although it is a metaphor, it seems to be a difficult saying." This kind of question has the greatest power, and he gave the examples of "If tigers and rhinos escape from the cage and tortoises and jades are destroyed in the box, whose fault is it?" (Analects) "People have walls to avoid evil. If the cracks in the wall are broken, whose fault is it?" (Zuo Zhuan).

Fifth, is antithetical metaphor. He said: "Fifth is antithetical metaphor, first comparing and then correcting, the top and bottom are consistent." And he gave the examples of "Fish forget each other in the rivers and lakes, and people forget each other in the art of Tao" (Zhuangzi), "Rumors stop with the wise" (Xunzi).

Sixth, is broad metaphor. He said: "Sixth is broad metaphor, taking it as a metaphor, not one is enough." And he gave the examples of "If you are gold, use you as a whetstone; if you are crossing a great river, use you as a boat; if there is a great drought, use you as rain" (Book of Documents), "Like pointing to the side of the river, like cutting millet with a spear, like poking a gourd with a cone."

Seventh, is simple metaphor. He said: "Seventh is simple metaphor, although the text is brief, the meaning is very clear." And he gave the examples of "One name is the vehicle of virtue" (Zuo Zhuan), "Benevolence is the home" (Fa Yan).

Eighth, is detailed metaphor. He said: "Eighth is detailed metaphor, which requires many words before the meaning is clear." And he gave the example of "Those who lure cicadas must focus on brightening the fire and shaking the tree, but if the fire is not bright, it is useless even if the tree is shaken; now if the ruler of men can brighten his virtue, the world will return to him, just like the cicadas returning to the fire." (Xunzi).

Ninth, is quoted metaphor. He said: "Ninth is quoted metaphor, citing previous words to prove the matter." And he gave the examples of "As the proverb says, sheltering him and then looking for an axe" (Zuo Zhuan) "Moth larvae follow the path of time, is this what it means?" (Book of Rites).

Tenth, is virtual metaphor. He said: "Tenth is virtual metaphor, which does not refer to things or events." And he gave the examples of "His words seem insufficient" (Analects), "Now it seems that there is no place to stop" (Laozi).

Of the ten items listed above, the third, analogy, the sixth, broad metaphor, the eighth, detailed metaphor, and the tenth, virtual metaphor, these four are all variations of direct metaphor and cannot be successful as a separate category; and the fifth, antithetical metaphor, and the seventh, simple metaphor, are just changes in hidden metaphor and cannot be independent; these places cannot but be said to have the problem of repetition. As the General Outline of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries says:

Dividing into categories is quite tedious and restrictive, and it is inevitable to abandon the big and seek the small. (To be continued)

Talks

Hankou Relief Society Expands its Organization 205

— Fang Jiu

The Hankou Municipal Government, considering the relief efforts in the city, although there are existing organizations such as the Relief Committee and the Poor People's Loan Office to handle them, believes that relief work, according to regulations, is not limited to one aspect. Matters such as caring for the elderly and weak, temporary repatriation, and organizing winter relief are all crucial. Omissions in the arrangements would be contrary to the government's principle of treating everyone equally. Therefore, to comprehensively plan and consider all aspects, aiming to universally benefit the poor, it has been decided to expand the organization of the existing Hankou Relief Committee. The committee will establish six departments for women, beggars, the disabled, orphans, infant care, and loans. Other relief efforts will also be handled by the committee, streamlining authority and particularly focusing on providing loans to the poor to help them find their own livelihoods, thereby stabilizing the city.

Originally, as the saying goes, "Help in emergencies, not in poverty." Helping the poor is indeed a very difficult task, especially now that our great country has suffered repeated enemy invasions, and rural bankruptcy seems to have made no progress under the slogan of "reviving the countryside." The expansion of the Hankou Municipal Government's Relief Committee is not without a traceable root cause.

On the surface, the expanded organization of the Hankou Relief Society seems to be a very welcome thing for the universal benefit of the poor. All those with a compassionate heart bless the poor, believing that the number of poor people can be reduced and society can be stabilized. Perhaps "living in peace and working happily" and "economic prosperity" can be achieved. However, according to actual observations, the expanded organization of the Hankou Relief Society precisely reveals the hidden worries of unrest in Hankou. Because no matter how much the organization of the Relief Society expands, the mass production of the poor may make the expanded organization of the Relief Society become a not-so-large organization.

We see the increasing number of beggars on the streets every day. Examining their origins, some have fled famine from disaster-stricken rural areas, while others have become unemployed and have no means of making a living. Others, such as women (prostitutes), the disabled, orphans, abandoned infants, etc., are all products of social and economic bankruptcy. Therefore, while the expansion of the "Relief Society" is necessary, it is even more "necessary" to ensure that slogans such as "prospering the market" and "reviving the countryside" are thoroughly and resolutely implemented!

As for loans to the poor, we have also organized them in Shanghai in the past, but the conditions were harsh, such as requiring a guarantor from a shop. May I ask, which shop trusts the poor? Therefore, loans to the poor only make the poor feel "overwhelmed with difficulties"! This point is deeply hoped that the philanthropists who organize loans to the poor will pay attention to.

On the Balcony 206

— Changfeng

I was awakened in the morning by a knocking sound. The weather was getting hot again, and I thought it would be good to get up early, so I slipped on my slippers and went to the balcony to wash up. However, upon opening the door, there were piles of wood and lead sheets in front of me. Two carpenters were working on the balcony, and the second landlord was standing high on the steps leading to the balcony, seemingly directing everything. When he saw me come out, he greeted me with a smile and told me that he was going to build a loft on the balcony to store some old things. Almost all of Shanghai's second landlords rely on renting out a shikumen building to make a living, and it is common to build lofts on the balcony. I casually responded, "Very good! Very good!" Although building a loft would at least reduce many conveniences for us tenants on the third floor with three rooms, the common living room when I moved in has now been turned into their bedroom, so the tenants on the third floor naturally have no reason to object to building a loft on the balcony.

When I came back in the evening, the two carpenters had just finished cleaning up. A loft with a lead sheet roof had been built, and it just covered the light behind my bedroom. I stepped onto the steps to take a look. The balcony still had a corner with a water tap. I don't have a wife, and my clothes are all sent to the laundry, so it is still convenient for me to have a water tap.

Page 20

It seemed to be about a week later. When I went to the balcony to wash up in the morning, I found that a family was living in the loft, a couple and a child. The man greeted me very politely and asked if I lived on the third floor, and was afraid that the child's noise had startled me. The man spoke very gently, as if he was very sorry. I told him that I usually got up very early, and put a basin of cold water and went back to the room. When I went downstairs that day, the second landlord deliberately stopped me and declared:

"A family has moved onto the balcony. They were introduced by a friend. Because all the rooms are full, I rented the balcony to them. My things are still piled at the foot of the stairs!"

As he spoke, he pointed to a pile of broken things under the stairs, as if he didn't mean to lend the lead sheet loft on the balcony to others, but that he had lent it out because he couldn't refuse the friend's request. He walked out.

A few days later, I gradually became familiar with the family on the balcony. The couple were both very good people. They were afraid that it would be inconvenient for me to fetch water, so they often filled the lead bucket outside my door with water for me. The man asked the second landlord several times if I disliked them, and sometimes came to my room to chat.

They both worked in a cigarette factory nearby. The woman worked the day shift, and the man worked the night shift, but sometimes when the two of them couldn't switch shifts, they would lock the child in the room. Once, he gave me many cigarettes, which he brought back from the factory. He said that he didn't smoke himself, and they would just get moldy if he left them. It is said that there is a rule in the cigarette factory that each employee is given a certain number of cigarettes every month. Those workers sell them to cigarette shops at a low price to earn some extra income. So I knew that "they would just get moldy if I left them" was his excuse. I was willing to sell those cigarettes to me at the market price, but he refused to take my money. And the cigarettes for the second month were given to me again. Since I couldn't refuse, I bought some candy and gave it to their child as a token of appreciation. He thanked me a thousand times.

The second landlord was originally afraid that I would not be used to living with those lower-class people and would want to move out. Now that he knew that we got along very well, he often came up to the third floor to join in. He said that I was a good tenant, and that the couple were also very good people, and that people who went out needed help from others, like a meddling matchmaker.

The second joint photography exhibition of Lu Shi Fu and Chen Chuanlin opened on the 20th on the fourth floor of the Da... Company. The one on the left is by Mr. Chen....

...The woman who worked the day shift had not returned, and the man, as usual, locked the door and went to work the night shift. He met me at the door and happily told me: "The factory is going to produce a batch of orders, and his mother has gone to work the day and night shifts. The extra pay for adding a shift is doubled, but unfortunately, there are not many times when shifts are added." He jumped downstairs like a child.

That night, I was awakened by a loud noise, and at the same time, someone was knocking on my door. It was the second landlord's voice. I put on my clothes and came out. A burst of heat scorched me. There were many people on the balcony knocking on the lead sheet. It turned out that the loft had caught fire. Because it was a lead sheet roof, the fire could not come out. The neighbors on the opposite building saw the fire in the small window and shouted. But many people were crowded in the corner of the balcony and there was no way to demolish the house, and there was no way to put out the fire. When the fire truck came and used an axe to open the loft, there was nothing left inside.

I looked at the scorched and smelly pile of fire, thinking of that lively child, that couple who were working the night shift in the factory! That kind couple. I leaned against my door as if I had lost consciousness until the smoke completely subsided before I felt a slight chill. The sky was about to dawn.

Night of the First Snow

On a snowy night in early winter, the master, young mistress, etc., are happily enjoying themselves under the warm light; but outside their window, a scene of the reality of the masses is also unfolding——

The situation is extremely tense and terrifying. Sandbags are piled high on the streets, and soldiers are wearing leather shoes and carrying guns, ready to sacrifice themselves to defend the nation and the truth. At this time, the unemployed poor and hawkers have to stand in the corner of the wall against the wind for the sake of life, sighing and resenting deeply.

He Laosan is an unemployed worker who has been running around for a day and borrowed two yuan; he is now standing on the street corner, waiting for another friend who is willing to lend him money. On one side, he is worried about his hungry wife and children at home. Standing beside him is the wandering Mr. Yu, a man of letters with nowhere to go. So the two of them talked and exchanged the sincere sympathy of the oppressed.

The street corner is really a public school full of life knowledge; the wonton seller tells of the suffering he has suffered from the economic panic; the thief tells of his way of life…………

A poor girl in distress, because the Northeast has become a lost country, and the enemy has taken away their peace, so she wandered to the coast of the Yangtze River with her old father, begging for food. However, everyone in the city is also shouting that they cannot live, chewing on the lodging expenses of poverty, and the inn waiter has detained his old father.

The poor girl pleads bitterly with the banker, but all she gets is ruthless disgust. The poor girl is overwhelmed by hunger and cold and faints on the ground. He Laosan couldn't stand it and instinctively used the one yuan he borrowed to pay off the poor girl's debt. But He Laosan lost the money to buy wontons. Finally, he got the sympathy of the wonton seller, who gave He Laosan and Mr. Yu wontons for free.

At that time, street singers wandered to this street corner. Among them, street singer A is a master of singing Qilin-style Peking Opera: street singer B is a frustrated vocalist. Because ladies and gentlemen do not understand art, he has no food to eat and is reduced to being an assistant to street singer A. Street singer B was discovered by Mr. Yu to be an old friend from many years ago, so everyone exchanged sighs.

He Laosan finally couldn't wait for his friend, but his wife rushed over anxiously, complaining about the suffering of not having money to pay the rent and the children having nothing to eat. She wanted to drag him home, because the enemy was about to carry out their beastly massacre.

But they didn't expect the enemy to rush over violently immediately. Even the masters and young mistresses did not expect it, and they were still dancing and singing amorous songs madly.

Finally, in order to survive and not to be inhuman slaves of a lost country, the masses united with the soldiers and fought bravely for the truth.

Storytelling 209

He Yunfang He Qinfang Double Pearl Ball

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Baochai Catching Butterflies"

Light clouds and drizzle, spring is brewing thick. Throw away idle worries and go to Emerald Pavilion. The eyes are full of fragrant flowers and birds are silent. Suddenly, a pair of butterflies chase after the fragrance. Fluttering like a flower ball. Up and down like birds entering the forest. He is, the wind occasionally carries swallows. When playing in the water, he wants to learn from dragonflies. Baochai is, carrying a silk fan and tapping lightly. But seeing, the sleeves are slightly fragrant and the sweat is dripping. Passing through the nine bends of the painting gallery. Parting flowers and willows are more careful. Just when, wanting to catch but suddenly inaccessible. Suddenly hearing, whispered words are heard across the water. Baochai is, always able to cheat with alertness. Walking across Qinfang Bridge, he hesitates. Loudly calling Pin'er on purpose. He is, shifting the blame to Jiangdong for fear of killing himself. Suddenly hearing the window blessing open. He then raised his voice and slowly stepped towards the water's edge. Xiaohong was very anxious when he heard it. From now on, he will plant a source of trouble to Xiaoxiang. It is a loss for him to put in a lot of effort.

Movie News

Epic "A Midsummer Night's Dream" 212

Premiering at the Grand Theater from Saturday

"Robin Hood" 213

Showing at the Great Shanghai

Warner Pictures, the authority in the American film industry, after more than two years of preparation, actually spent 1.5 million gold dollars of capital and exhausted the efforts of thousands of people to put Shakespeare's great poetic drama "A Midsummer Night's Dream" on the screen. Since its release, it has been welcomed everywhere. Even at the previous Cathay Grand Theater in this city, the highest price was as high as four yuan, but it was still full every night, which shows how popular the film is. It is now heard that the Grand Theater has scheduled to premiere this film starting this Saturday, and in order to make it popular, the price will not be increased as before. It is expected that it will cause a sensation again at that time.

Shirley Temple's New Work 214

After the little darling Shirley Temple's new work The Pool Rich Cirj after "Little Miss Marker" has now been completed. The contract with Fox Company in 1935 has expired, and a new contract has been renewed. The weekly salary has increased from 2,500 to 4,500 gold dollars, and four films are made each year. The price of each film is about 45,000 gold dollars, while the old contract was only 20,000 yuan per film. The difference before and after is more than doubled. The speed of progress is rare among other stars. The new film to be made will be Dimples. It will be filmed after the summer vacation.

"Electric Sound" Volume 5, Issue 24 Published 215

"Electric Sound" has reached its fifth spring since its publication. Its timely news, accurate reviews, abundant text, and touching photos have long been loved by the general public. It is heard that the 24th issue of the fifth volume has been published recently, and its content is even richer and more substantial, such as "Lianhua actor You Yufu ...", "Moonlight's public ... detailed information on the release", "Li Lin ... the deformed development of the room", "Yuan Meiling's head ... cover", "Chaplin's car accident and injury", "Qin Harrow's experience with men" and dozens of other articles, all of which are new and strange news that has been heard outside. As for its cover and ... picture, they are all original negatives that have been published from ..., which are beautiful and worth seeing. It is really a beloved reading material that movie fans cannot miss. Each book still sells for 9 cents in French currency. All bookstores and newspapers ... are selling them. Add 5 cents for postage for letters. Send them to "Sanhe Publishing House, 138 Nanjing Road, Shanghai" and they will be sent immediately.
